  to the same fixed monoid set. So the honest inventory of arche's real
  data-parallel surface is map / each / system + reduce + sort (+ scan pending),
  all with builtin monoids only ‚ÄĒ no custom-operator folds.

‚úĽ Cogitated for 38s

‚ÄĽ recap: We're exploring whether arche could forbid control flow in data-parallel leaves (keeping it in funcs/policies), grounded in the real arche-rpg and server code. Next: decide if that branchless-leaves rule plus a custom-monoid scan are worth specifying as actual language features. (disable recaps in /config)

‚ĚĮ so can the branchless stuff still be useful if a bunch of branches are used   
  in functions                                                                  

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ and this is the distinction I should have led with. "Branchless leaf"
  buys two different things, and func-branches only touch one of them:

  1. Branchless between elements/systems ‚ÄĒ no data-dependent control flow
  decides which rows run, in what order, with what dependencies. This is what
  gives parallelism + static scheduling + placement legality (the ¬ß5 win).
  Func-internal branches don't touch this at all ‚ÄĒ they're inside one element's
  computation, invisible to the schedule.

  2. Branchless within an element ‚ÄĒ no divergent branch inside one element's
  work. This is SIMD/GPU lane efficiency. Branchy funcs do affect this ‚ÄĒ but
  only as a performance cost, only on GPU, and only for genuinely-divergent
  branches.

  Concrete:

  arche
  classify :: func(x: int) -> int {        // branchy pure func ‚ÄĒ fine, funcs
  allow control flow
    if x < 0  { return 0 }
    if x < 10 { return 1 }
    return 2
  }

  step :: map (query { pos, bucket }) {    // branchless LEAF
    bucket = classify(pos.x);              // calls the branchy func per element
  }

  What survives despite classify branching:
  - Scheduling: step's signature is "reads pos, writes bucket." That
  parallelizes it against other systems and orders it in the schedule.
  classify's ifs are invisible to the scheduler. Full cross-system parallelism ‚ÄĒ
  preserved.
  - Bounded static cost: the loop runs exactly row_count times; cost ‚Č§ rows √ó
  worst-case classify. Still computable ‚Üí still statically placeable.
  - Columnar/SoA access: unaffected.
  - CPU vectorization: classify's < compares are predicable ‚ÄĒ the compiler
  if-converts them to selects, so even this "branchy" func is branchless after
  lowering. Most clamp/threshold/bucket branches are this kind.

  Where func-branches actually bite: only when the branch is not predicable ‚ÄĒ a
  data-dependent loop, or heavy unbalanced arms ‚ÄĒ and only when the leaf is
  placed on the GPU, where it costs lane efficiency (divergence). It never costs
  correctness and never costs CPU placement.

  So: a leaf calling branchy funcs is still a flat, parallel,
  statically-scheduled, GPU-legal kernel. The branches inside funcs only grade
  how efficiently it runs on wide hardware ‚ÄĒ which is exactly the job of that
  "straight-line vs branchy" color on funcs: it tells the placer "this leaf's
  funcs predicate cleanly ‚Üí GPU-profitable" vs "this one diverges ‚Üí keep on
  CPU." The branchless-leaf discipline holds; func branches just partition
  GPU-profitability, not legality.

‚úĽ Cooked for 51s

‚ĚĮ so should we ban control flow in a system. Or make it a flag like eff         

‚óŹ Make it a hard flag, defaulting to off ‚ÄĒ which is a ban, just with a marked
  opt-out. The "ban vs flag" framing is a false binary, and the flag version
  dominates:

  - A system without the flag is forbidden from data-dependent control flow
  (generalize map's E0046 to every unflagged leaf ‚ÄĒ a hard error, not a lint).
  So no-flag systems get the identical guarantee an absolute ban would give:
  branchless, cost-exact, GPU-legal, placer reads it from the signature
  (separate compilation holds).
  - A system with the flag keeps control flow ‚ÄĒ the honest escape hatch for the
  one case the flat-effect model says is irreducible: the monadic tail
  (result-dependent effect sequencing, ¬ß5/¬ß8). Flagged ‚áí the placer knows "CPU,
  not cost-exact." No surprise.

  An absolute ban only beats this if no irreducible case exists ‚ÄĒ and the model
  explicitly says one does (the framed-read / handle_msg tail). So the absolute
  ban buys nothing over the default-off flag except removing the escape you'll
  occasionally need.

  It also pairs cleanly with eff and reconstructs your kinds as flag
  combinations ‚ÄĒ the "just system" unification:

  system Q (muts)              // no eff, no ctl  ‚Üí branchless leaf  (today's
  `map`, GPU-placeable)
  system Q (muts) ctl          // ctl, no eff     ‚Üí pure divergent kernel (CPU,
  or GPU-with-divergence)
  system Q (muts) eff          // eff, no ctl     ‚Üí straight-line effect leaf
  system Q (muts) eff ctl      // both            ‚Üí the imperative monadic tail
  (CPU)

  eff gates running effects; the new flag (call it ctl or seq) gates
  data-dependent control flow in the body. Both hard, both signature-visible,
  both consumed by the placer.

  Two conditions worth stating:
  1. Make it hard, not advisory ‚ÄĒ absence of ctl is a checkable prohibition
  (E0046-generalized), so the placer can rely on it. A soft "might be slow" hint
  would be exactly the noise your ethos rejects.
  2. The flag is also a measurement. Count ctl systems over real programs. If
  the set collapses to only genuinely-irreducible monadic tails (and the
  selective layer whenS/ifS absorbs the rest), you've empirically earned the
  right to promote it to an absolute ban later. Start with the flag; let the
  data tell you if ban is reachable.

  So: hard ctl flag, default off, paired with eff. That's a ban for every system
  that doesn't raise it, plus an honest, placement-visible opt-out for the tail
  you can't yet remove.

‚úĽ Baked for 1m 30s

‚ĚĮ monadic  tail shouldn't have an escape hatch, it should mean a redesign       

‚óŹ Then it's a ban, no flag ‚ÄĒ and my escape-hatch was the wrong instinct. The
  monadic tail was never irreducible; ECS decomposition is its reduction. So
  there was no case the flag was protecting ‚ÄĒ "needs the flag" just meant
  "hasn't been decomposed yet." Banning it makes the decomposition mandatory,
  which is the point.

  So the rule is the same character as system-can't-call-system: control flow in
  a leaf is unspellable, not @allow-able. Hitting it is a compile error that
  means "restructure," exactly as hitting a system-calling-a-system does.

  What a system/each body collapses to under the ban:
  - run effects, straight-line + assign columns/locals from results
  - conditional effects ‚Üí selective values (whenS/ifS), not body ifs ‚ÄĒ a
  function call, not control flow
  - pure branching/looping ‚Üí a func (its legitimate home; recursion is free
  there)
  - result-dependent sequencing ‚Üí decompose: state column + producer/consumer +
  tick boundary. The "then" becomes the next tick.

  No if/for in any leaf. The only branch-related construct left in the whole
  language is the straight-line/branchy color on funcs (for GPU-placement
  decidability) ‚ÄĒ not a system flag.

  The bill, so this isn't just agreement:

  1. The selective layer must be finished first. The flat-effect doc has only
  the guard form wired (whenS, ifS with a pure else); value-producing ifS is
  "the next step." Banning body control flow has nowhere to put legitimate
  static conditionals until that lands. This ban depends on completing it.
  2. ECS decomposition becomes mandatory, and you pay its cost every time (¬ß8):
  a state column, a producer + consumer system, and one tick of latency per 
  state transition, plus the max-reserved buffers. The framed read goes from a
  4-line inline loop to a state-machine-as-data spread across systems. Accepted
  under your stance, but it's a real, recurring cost ‚ÄĒ not free.
  3. This changes the flat-effect doc's current position. ¬ß5/¬ß8 today explicitly
  permit the monadic tail to live inline in a flat system/each as an "honest
  cost." The ban rewrites that to "monadic tail = redesign trigger ‚Üí decompose,"
  and the one sanctioned holdout (csv.load under @allow(proc_not_primitive))
  has to actually become the pending "archetype-targeted load system" rather
  than stay opted-out ‚ÄĒ otherwise the no-escape-hatch rule has an escape hatch.

  Net: ban control flow in all leaves (hard, unspellable), branch-color on funcs
  only, monadic tail forced to ECS decomposition. The two prerequisites are
  finishing the selective layer and accepting the per-transition tick-latency of
  decomposition everywhere.

‚úĽ Cooked for 1m 5s

‚ĚĮ 1. ok                                                                         
                                                                                
  2. show me, because I don't see it                                            

‚óŹ Let me ground this in real primitives before I write it ‚ÄĒ I don't want to hand
  you more fabricated syntax. Checking what arche actually has for branchless
  predication and row routing:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Verified primitives first: select(cond,a,b) is real
  (tests/unit/gpu/physics_step.arche:15), and mask-arithmetic is the documented
  "Conditional Behavior" idiom ‚ÄĒ vel = vel * (pos > 10) (README), Row.price = 
  Row.price * (Row.quantity > 0). So comparisons yield 0/1 you multiply with.
  That's all I need.

  BANNED ‚ÄĒ inline monadic (what we're removing):

  arche
  handle :: each (query { fd, ok }) {
    hdr: [1]char;
    read(fd, hdr, 1)(got:, err:);
    if err != 0 || got == 0 { ok = 0; return; }   // branch + early return
    len := int(hdr[0]);
    body: [256]char;
    read(fd, body, len)(got:, err:);                // read #2 SHAPED BY read
  #1's result
    ok = (err == 0 && got == len);
  }

  DECOMPOSED ‚ÄĒ state as data, one branchless step per tick. States linear so
  "phase complete" = +1: NEED_HDR=0, NEED_BODY=1, DONE=2. The trick that kills
  the state-branch: bytes to request = want - have uniformly (want is HDR in
  phase 0, HDR+len in phase 1).

  arche
  // advance EVERY connection one step. No if, no early return ‚ÄĒ select + masks
  only.
  advance :: each (query { fd, state, want, have, buf }) {
    going := (state < DONE);                 // 1 while unfinished, else 0
  (mask)
    req   := (want - have) * going;          // bytes to pull; 0 once DONE
  (mask)
    recv(fd, req)(buf, got:);                // non-blocking; got = bytes read
  (data, not control)
    have   = have + got;

    was_hdr   := (state == NEED_HDR);        // mask, BEFORE advancing
    done_now  := (have >= want) * going;     // finished this phase this tick?
  (mask)
    want   = select(done_now * was_hdr, HDR + body_len(buf), want);  // re-arm
  `want` on header completion
    state  = state + done_now;               // 0‚Üí1 (hdr), 1‚Üí2 (body); never
  past DONE
  }

  Trace it: phase 0 reads until have>=HDR ‚Üí done_now=1, was_hdr=1 ‚Üí want becomes
  HDR+body_len(buf), state‚Üí1. Phase 1 reads until have>=want ‚Üí want unchanged,
  state‚Üí2. At DONE, going=0 so req=0, recv(fd,0) is a no-op, done_now=0, state
  stays 2. Fully branchless ‚ÄĒ every connection runs the identical straight-line
  body. body_len is a pure func (branchy inside is fine), computed every tick
  (wasted unless the header just completed ‚ÄĒ the predication "pay the ceiling"
  cost).

  Response ‚ÄĒ conditional effect as a value, not control flow:

  arche
  reply :: each (query { fd, state, buf, want }) {
    resp := build_response(buf, want);                 // pure func ‚Üí Eff
    whenS(state == DONE, send_all(fd, resp))(_:, _:);   // fires iff DONE;
  selective rung, not an `if`
  }

  The schedule ‚ÄĒ this is where your "then" went:

  arche
  #run forever(seq({ accept_step, advance, reply, evict }))

  The monadic read#1 then read#2 is now advance re-run each tick. A two-phase
  message takes ‚Č•2 ticks; a slow body takes one recv per tick until full. The 
  sequencing became loop iteration ‚ÄĒ that's the per-tick latency cost, paid for
  every connection, in exchange for zero control flow and a flat parallel each.

  The one honest residue ‚ÄĒ eviction. A DONE connection sits in the pool getting
  no-op'd by the masks forever. Removing it per-row wants an if delete.
  Branchless options: (a) leave them ‚ÄĒ the masks make them free no-ops, wasteful
  but branchless; (b) evict does a batch compaction (a collective that
  partitions DONE rows out), not per-row control flow. You do not get clean
  per-row eviction without either a branch or a predicated-delete primitive that
  doesn't exist today. So lifecycle eviction is the place a branch genuinely
  wants back, and the branchless answer is "batch it, don't branch per row."

  So: the read-then-read sequencing decomposes cleanly to a branchless per-tick
  select+mask step (verified primitives), the completion condition lives in
  whenS (the selective layer you already accepted must land), and the only
  residue is row eviction ‚Üí batch compaction. No if/for, no early return, no
  inline monadic sequencing ‚ÄĒ at the cost of a tick per recv and some predicated
  wasted work.
‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 2m 51s

‚ĚĮ why if delete? why not whenS?                                                 

‚óŹ You're right ‚ÄĒ I was inconsistent. delete is an effect (structural mutation,
  the deferred command-buffer primitive ‚ÄĒ flat-effect ¬ß4), the exact same
  category as send. So the selective rung gates it identically:

  arche
  evict :: each (query { state, sent } as r) {
    whenS(state == DONE && sent == 1, delete(r))(_:);   // predicated delete,
  not an `if`
  }

  There's no reason eviction is special, and "needs an if delete or batch
  compaction" was wrong. whenS(cond, delete(r)) lowers to a guarded emit into
  the deferred command buffer, which flushes deleted rows at the stage barrier ‚ÄĒ
  which is precisely the mechanism arche already uses for per-row insert/delete
  (¬ß4, ¬ß6.2). Deferred flush also sidesteps iterator invalidation: you're not
  mutating the pool mid-iteration, you're collecting delete-commands and
  applying them at the seam. And it's the guard form of the selective (whenS,
  unit effect), so it's in the already-wired subset ‚ÄĒ no dependency on the
  unfinished value-producing ifS.

  So the corrected picture: the entire framed-read decomposition is branchless 
  with no residue.
  - advance ‚ÄĒ select + masks
  - reply ‚ÄĒ whenS(state==DONE, send)
  - evict ‚ÄĒ whenS(done && sent, delete(r))

  No if, no for, no per-row control flow anywhere. Batch compaction isn't needed
  ‚ÄĒ it's just an optional optimization if the predicated command-buffer churn
  (deletes evaluated every tick) gets expensive. The only real costs remain what
  they were: per-tick latency (a recv per tick) and predicated wasted work
  (conditions evaluated for every row every tick). I over-claimed a branch
  residue that the selective layer already covers.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 38s

‚ĚĮ does it have to be a seperate system now then                                 

‚óŹ No ‚ÄĒ they collapse into one branchless each. Once conditionality is
  whenS/select (values, not control flow), there's nothing to call between them,
  so advance + reply + evict are just three groups of effects on the same row
  in one body:

  arche
  tick :: each (query { fd, state, want, have, buf } as r) {
    going    := (state < DONE);
    req      := (want - have) * going;
    recv(fd, req)(buf, got:);  have = have + got;
    was_hdr  := (state == NEED_HDR);
    done_now := (have >= want) * going;
    want   = select(done_now * was_hdr, HDR + body_len(buf), want);
    state  = state + done_now;

    whenS(state == DONE, send_all(fd, build_response(buf, want)))(_:, _:);  //
  reply
    whenS(state == DONE, delete(r))(_:);                                     //
  evict, same tick
  }

  Send runs inline, delete(r) defers to the barrier ‚ÄĒ so a connection that
  finishes this tick replies and gets queued for removal in the same pass. You
  don't even need the sent flag: it only existed to avoid re-sending across 
  ticks, and now reply+evict co-occur.

  You only need a separate system when a stage barrier is semantically required:
  1. a deferred insert/delete must be applied before the next step reads the
  changed pool membership (e.g. step B iterates rows step A inserted),
  2. a cross-row reduction/sort must complete before the next step,
  3. the next step queries a different archetype/pool.

  None of those hold between advance‚Üíreply‚Üíevict on the same Conn row, so it's
  one each.

  The reframe that matters: the decomposition spreads work across ticks, not 
  across systems. The framed read went from one monadic handle each to one
  branchless tick each ‚ÄĒ same system count. What replaced the read#1 then read#2
  sequencing is the forever loop re-running tick, not extra systems. So "ECS
  decomposition" overstated it for the self-contained case:
  producer/consumer-across-systems is only forced when a monadic step must be
  shared between systems or hits one of those three barriers. A self-contained
  framed read is just "reify state into columns + loop one branchless each." The
  cost is purely the per-tick latency, not added systems.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 57s

‚ĚĮ so is this objectively slower                                                 

‚óŹ Honest answer: on a CPU, yes ‚ÄĒ measurably slower, and the slowdown buys you 
  nothing there. It's faster only in the regime branchless is actually for,
  which a TCP server isn't in. Here's the real accounting.

  What the branchless version adds:
  - Per-tick rescan ‚ÄĒ tick iterates every active connection each loop, reloading
  state columns, whether or not data arrived. O(conns) work per tick regardless
  of activity.
  - Polling syscalls ‚ÄĒ a recv per connection per tick, most returning 0/EAGAIN
  on idle conns. Syscall overhead (hundreds of ns‚Äď¬Ķs) dominates everything else
  here.
  - Predicated waste ‚ÄĒ body_len(buf) and build_response(...) computed every tick
  even when the row isn't at that phase; conditions evaluated for every row
  every tick.

  What it removes: the branches. And on a modern CPU those were nearly free ‚ÄĒ a
  connection sits in NEED_BODY across many recvs, so the state branch is highly
  predictable (~0 extra cycles); a misprediction is ~15‚Äď20 cycles and rare.
  You're spending syscall-and-rescan overhead (¬Ķs) to delete branches that cost
  ~nothing (cycles). Net loss.

  So for the server on a CPU: the inline version + readiness (epoll tells you
  which fds have data, so you touch only ready connections) wins clearly ‚ÄĒ no
  rescan, no polling, no predicated waste, and its branches are cheap. The
  branchless rewrite is slower, and the thing it buys (uniform, divergence-free,
  statically-costed execution) cashes out as zero because nothing here goes
  wide.

  Where it would be faster ‚ÄĒ the regime branchless is designed for:
  - SIMD/GPU, where a divergent branch wastes whole lanes (15‚Äď30√ó a predicted
  CPU branch) and predication is the only way to keep lanes full;
  - massive lockstep populations (packet/stream processing at millions of
  elements) where mispredictions, not syscalls, dominate.

  A connection FSM over a few thousand sockets on a CPU is neither.

  This is the blunt landing of the whole thread: branchless isn't a speed 
  technique, it's a placement technique. It makes a kernel cost-exact and
  GPU-legal. On a CPU with a good branch predictor, branches are cheap, so
  reifying them into select/masks/ticks is pure overhead ‚ÄĒ you pay for a
  property you never spend. The framed-read-as-branchless-FSM is the right shape
  only if you were going to run that FSM on a GPU/SIMD across a huge
  population. For an ordinary server, the inline branchy event loop is both
  simpler and faster.

  So the rule from earlier holds, now with the cost attached: reify control flow
  into data only for the kernels you'll actually place wide. Everywhere else,
  branches belong in funcs/systems and run on the CPU, because there they're
  free.

     ‚Ēā (not yet the law) of docs/design/the-flat-effect-model.md ¬ß5/¬ß8. The    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā goal is                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā to record what is now known before it's lost, keeping the doc's         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā BEFORE/PROPOSED                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā convention and its honest-caveats tone. Doc-only change. Nothing in     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā code,                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tests, or the landed flat-effect law changes yet.                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The four things now known:                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Branch-freedom is granted by the kind/signature (an explicit ask),   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā derived from the body (an inferred color). Legality is declared;        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā profitability is derived.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed technique. On a CPU ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā with                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a branch predictor, branches are ~free; reifying control flow into data ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pure overhead unless the kernel is placed wide (SIMD/GPU divergence) or ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs static cost.                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. Control flow in leaves is banned (hard, unspellable, no flag, no     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā escape                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hatch). The monadic tail is not irreducible ‚ÄĒ it decomposes.            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Branch-ness is                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a color on funcs only (for GPU-placement decidability).                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4. The monadic tail decomposes to state-as-data + one branchless each   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tick (not separate systems); the cost is per-tick latency and is        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā objectively slower on a CPU ‚ÄĒ right only when placed wide.              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Edits to docs/wip/migration-derived-placement.md                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā All additions reuse the existing BEFORE/PROPOSED convention and         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā verified arche                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā primitives (select(c,a,b) ‚ÄĒ tests/unit/gpu/physics_step.arche:15;       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mask-arithmetic x * (a >= b) ‚ÄĒ README "Conditional Behavior",           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tests/unit/language/types/int_mask_times_float_column.arche; whenS      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā guard                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā form; deferred insert/delete command buffer).                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Revise ¬ß0 and ¬ß5 ‚ÄĒ "derived from the body" ‚Üí "granted by the kind"   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - ¬ß0: change the framing that branch-freedom is derived by inspecting   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā body. For a map/leaf it is guaranteed by the kind you asked for         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (E0046). Add one line: deriving access/branch facts from the body       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā breaks                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā separate compilation and re-introduces the "inferred color" the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā flat-effect                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā doc condemns; the placer must read the signature (query + mutables +    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā eff),                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not the body ‚ÄĒ exactly how Bevy schedules from query types, never       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bodies.                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - ¬ß5: add the legality vs profitability split. Legality (can this go    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wide?)                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā = the explicit kind/signature ask, no body analysis, no research.       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Profitability (should it?) = the static cost model ‚ÄĒ the genuinely open ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā part.                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā This shrinks ¬ß5's unsolved cell to only the cost decision.              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. New section "¬ß6 Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā technique"                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Content:                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - CPU branch predictor makes well-predicted branches ~0 cycles;         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mispredict                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ~15‚Äď20. State/loop branches in real kernels are highly predictable.     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Reifying control flow into data                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (select/masks/transition-tables/per-tick                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ticks) is pure overhead on a CPU ‚ÄĒ you pay rescans, predicated waste,   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (for I/O FSMs) polling syscalls to remove branches that were nearly     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā free.                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - It pays only where branches are genuinely expensive: SIMD/GPU lane    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā divergence (15‚Äď30√ó a predicted CPU branch) or pathological              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā misprediction at                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā scale (stream/packet processing of millions of elements in lockstep).   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Rule: reify control flow into data only for kernels you will place    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wide.                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Everywhere else, branches belong in funcs/systems and run on the CPU.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Note: the transition-table-as-value + parallel-scan FSM               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (simdjson-style) is                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not expressible today ‚ÄĒ scan is an unimplemented Phase-2 spec           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (tests/unit/language/collectives/scan_int.arche:2) and its operator is  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a                                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fixed monoid set (semantic.c:2496), so custom-operator scan would be a  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā real                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā feature, not a design idiom. Mark as such.                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. New section "¬ß7 Control flow in leaves is banned; the monadic tail   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā decomposes"                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Content:                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Rule: generalize map's E0046 to every data-parallel leaf ‚ÄĒ control    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā flow                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā in a leaf is a hard error, unspellable, no flag and no @allow (same     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā character as system-cannot-call-system). Hitting it means redesign.     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Branch-ness becomes a color on funcs (straight-line vs branchy),      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā readable from the func signature, so a leaf's GPU-placeability is       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā decidable                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā from signatures alone (separate compilation). A branchy func taints its ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā caller's GPU efficiency only ‚ÄĒ never CPU placement, never correctness.  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Where control flow goes instead: pure branching/looping ‚Üí a func;     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā conditional effects ‚Üí selective values (whenS/ifS); result-dependent    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sequencing ‚Üí decompose (state-as-data + tick).                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Worked example: the framed read (BANNED inline monadic handle ‚Üí       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā branchless tick). Include the verified-primitive version:               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā going := (state < DONE), req := (want-have)*going, uniform recv,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā done_now := (have>=want)*going, want = select(done_now*was_hdr, ...),   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā state = state + done_now; reply + evict via                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā whenS(state==DONE, send_all(...)) and whenS(state==DONE, delete(r))     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (delete IS a structural-mutation effect ‚Üí the selective rung gates it;  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā deferred command buffer flushes at the barrier).                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - It collapses to ONE each, not separate systems. Separate systems are  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā forced only by a real barrier: deferred insert/delete must land before  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā next step reads pool membership; a cross-row reduction/sort must        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā complete; or                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a different archetype. None hold here. Decomposition spreads across     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ticks,                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not systems ‚ÄĒ same system count as the inline version.                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Honest cost (cross-ref ¬ß6): on a CPU this is objectively slower ‚ÄĒ     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per-tick rescan, polling syscalls, predicated waste ‚ÄĒ and buys nothing  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā there;                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it is right only when the FSM is placed wide.                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Prerequisites / consequences: the selective layer must be finished    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (value-producing ifS, not just the wired guard form); this changes the  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā flat-effect doc's ¬ß5/¬ß8 position (which currently permits the monadic   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tail                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā inline as an "honest cost") to "monadic tail = redesign trigger ‚Üí       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā decompose";                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and the one sanctioned holdout (csv.load under                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā @allow(proc_not_primitive))                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā must become the pending archetype-targeted load system, else the        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no-escape                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rule has an escape.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4. Short note "¬ß8 The permission signature (one system, kinds as        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā presets)"                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - One system kind carrying a permission signature: read set (the        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā query),                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā write set (the (mutables) list ‚ÄĒ hoisted out of the named/shared query, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unlike Bevy's per-system &mut), and the eff flag. Kinds (map/each) are  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā named flag-presets over this signature, not primitives.                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Because leaves are branchless by ban, there is no branch flag on      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā leaves ‚ÄĒ the leaf/func boundary is the gate, and branch-ness lives only ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā as                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the func color (¬ß7).                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

‚ĚĮ branch freedom should probably be derived from CPU vs GPU or no               

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ that's cleaner than what I had, and it means dropping the "explicit ask
  for branch power" framing entirely. The key realization: "branchless" and 
  "GPU-eligible" are the same fact. There's no independent branch property to
  declare or ask for ‚ÄĒ branch-ness is just which end of the CPU/GPU axis you're 
  on:

  - branchy ‚Üí CPU-only (branches are free there anyway)
  - branchless ‚Üí GPU-eligible (then cost decides if it actually goes)

  So branch-freedom is derived, not declared ‚ÄĒ it's a consequence of the
  placement axis, exactly as you're saying. You don't ask "may I branch?"; you
  write code, and whether it branches is what places it.

  One sharpening: GPU-eligibility isn't branch-freedom alone ‚ÄĒ it's a bundle:
  branchless ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß bounded. Branch-freedom is one conjunct. eff knocks
  you to CPU; an unbounded/data-dependent loop knocks you to CPU; a branch
  knocks you to CPU. Cost then picks among whatever's left eligible. So the
  placer derives one predicate over the kernel ‚ÄĒ "GPU-eligible?" ‚ÄĒ and
  branch-freedom is folded into it, not a separate flag.

  The one fork this exposes (and it's the real decision): deriving the branch
  requirement from placement makes it a whole-program fact. Since leaves are
  banned from control flow (prior conclusion), the only branch-ness left is in
  funcs ‚ÄĒ and a func must be branchless iff a GPU-placed leaf calls it. That
  depends on the caller's placement:

  - Whole-program placement ‚ÄĒ derive everything (a func's branch requirement
  follows from whether any GPU-placed caller reaches it). Pure derivation, zero
  declarations, matches your "derived from CPU vs GPU" instinct exactly. Cost:
  you need the whole program; no separate compilation of placement.
  - Separate compilation ‚ÄĒ you can't see the caller's placement, so you must
  surface the func's branch-ness as a signature fact (the color) to decide
  placement per-unit. A small declared bit, the price of separate compilation.

  So the honest statement: branch-freedom is derived from CPU-vs-GPU (you're
  right, it's not an ask) ‚ÄĒ unless you want separate compilation, in which case
  the one derived bit has to be visible in the signature so each unit can be
  placed without its callers. Which way depends on whether placement needs to be
  separately compilable.

  I'll revise the doc plan: ¬ß1 changes from "granted by the kind, explicit ask"
  to "branch-freedom = GPU-eligibility, derived from the placement axis; the
  only open choice is whole-program derivation vs surfacing the one bit for
  separate compilation." Want me to fold that in and which side of the sep-comp
  fork should the doc take?

‚úĽ Baked for 1m 30s

‚ĚĮ we need seperate compilation for dev only so it probably doesn't have to be   
  completely accurate and having it explicitly decided just  for dev would be   
  annoying                                                                      

‚óŹ That resolves the fork by dissolving it ‚ÄĒ and it reinforces the "no
  annotations" thesis. The key fact that makes your call sound: placement is a 
  performance decision, not a correctness one. A kernel computes the same result
  on CPU or GPU; CPU is always legal. So:

  - Dev = CPU-only. Everything is CPU-legal, so dev needs zero placement
  analysis and zero declarations ‚ÄĒ each unit compiles independently for CPU,
  trivially separately-compilable. The branch-freedom question simply never
  arises in dev, because on the CPU branches are free. "Approximate" isn't even
  a compromise here ‚ÄĒ CPU is exact for results, just not optimized.
  - Release = whole-program. GPU placement (derive branchless ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß 
  bounded + the cost model) happens only in the optimized build, where you have
  the whole program anyway ‚ÄĒ so it's fully derived, never declared.

  So the signature-color option is cut. It only existed to make GPU placement
  separately-compilable, and dev doesn't do GPU placement, so nobody needs it.
  No branch/placement annotations anywhere: dev sidesteps the question, release
  derives it whole-program. Exactly your instinct ‚ÄĒ branch-freedom derived from
  CPU-vs-GPU, and the dev/release split means you never pay for it explicitly.

  One honest flag: dev-on-CPU means GPU placement and any GPU-specific behavior
  (float precision, divergence perf) isn't exercised until release/perf builds.
  That's a normal dev/release tradeoff ‚ÄĒ you iterate logic on CPU, validate
  placement in release ‚ÄĒ but worth stating so it's not a surprise.

  Let me fold this into the doc plan and re-exit for approval.

     edit
     Update WIP doc with the branchless / control-flow / placement conclusions

     Context

     A long design discussion (this session) reached firm conclusions about how
     branchlessness, control flow, the monadic tail, and CPU/GPU placement
     relate in
     arche's derived-placement model. These sharpen ‚ÄĒ and in places correct ‚ÄĒ
     the WIP
     doc docs/wip/migration-derived-placement.md, and they amend the position
     (not yet the law) of docs/design/the-flat-effect-model.md ¬ß5/¬ß8. Goal:
     record
     what is now known, keeping the doc's BEFORE/PROPOSED convention and
     honest-caveats
     tone. Doc-only change. No code, tests, or landed law changes yet.

     What is now known:
     1. Branch-freedom = GPU-eligibility ‚ÄĒ it is derived, not an ask.
     "Branchless"
     and "GPU-eligible" are the same fact; there is no independent branch
     permission to declare. GPU-eligibility is a bundle: branchless ‚ąß 
     effect-free ‚ąß bounded. Cost picks among eligible placements. (Drops the
     earlier
     "explicit ask for branch power" / "granted by the kind" framing.)
     2. Placement is a performance decision, not correctness. A kernel yields
     the
     same result on CPU or GPU; CPU is always legal. So placement can be wrong
     (slow) without being incorrect.
     3. Dev/release split removes all placement annotations. Dev = CPU-only,
     trivially separately-compilable, zero placement analysis, zero declarations
     (branches are free on CPU, so the question never arises). Release =
     whole-program, fully derived GPU placement. No branch/placement annotations
     anywhere. The signature-color-for-separate-compilation idea is cut ‚ÄĒ only
     GPU placement needed it, and dev does no GPU placement.
     4. Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed technique. On a CPU
     with
     a branch predictor, branches are ~free; reifying control flow into data
     (select/masks/tables/per-tick ticks) is pure overhead unless the kernel is
     placed wide (SIMD/GPU divergence) or needs static cost.
     5. Control flow in leaves is banned (hard, unspellable, no flag, no escape
     hatch). The monadic tail is not irreducible ‚ÄĒ it decomposes to
     state-as-data
       - one branchless each per tick (not separate systems). Cost: per-tick
     latency, objectively slower on a CPU ‚ÄĒ right only when placed wide.

     Edits to docs/wip/migration-derived-placement.md

     Reuse the BEFORE/PROPOSED convention and verified primitives (select(c,a,b)
     ‚ÄĒ
     tests/unit/gpu/physics_step.arche:15; mask-arithmetic x * (a >= b) ‚ÄĒ README
     "Conditional Behavior",
     tests/unit/language/types/int_mask_times_float_column.arche;
     whenS guard form; deferred insert/delete command buffer).

     1. Revise ¬ß0 and ¬ß5 ‚ÄĒ branch-freedom is derived GPU-eligibility, not a 
     body-sniff "ask"

     - ¬ß0: replace "branch-free, so a GPU candidate (derived from the body)"
     with:
     branch-freedom is GPU-eligibility ‚ÄĒ one fact, the CPU/GPU axis itself, not
     an independent property to ask for. GPU-eligibility = branchless ‚ąß 
     effect-free ‚ąß bounded; the placer derives this one predicate.
     - ¬ß5: add the legality vs profitability split. Legality (GPU-eligible?) is
     a
     trivial derived predicate over the unit. Profitability (should it go?) is
     the
     static cost model ‚ÄĒ the genuinely open research cell. This shrinks ¬ß5's
     unsolved part to only the cost decision.

     2. New section "¬ß6 Dev/release placement ‚ÄĒ no annotations, ever"

     - Placement is performance, not correctness; CPU is always legal and exact
     for
     results.
     - Dev = CPU-only: trivially separately-compilable, no cross-module
     placement
     analysis, no declarations. Fast iteration; the branch question never
     arises.
     - Release = whole-program: GPU placement fully derived (branchless ‚ąß 
     effect-free ‚ąß bounded + cost), no author annotations.
     - Honest flag: GPU placement / GPU-specific behavior (float precision,
     divergence perf) is exercised only in release/perf builds ‚ÄĒ a normal
     dev/release tradeoff (iterate logic on CPU, validate placement in release).

     3. New section "¬ß7 Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed 
     technique"

     - CPU branch predictor: well-predicted branch ~0 cycles, mispredict ~15‚Äď20;
     state/loop branches in real kernels are highly predictable.
     - Reifying control flow into data is pure overhead on a CPU (rescans,
     predicated waste, polling syscalls for I/O FSMs) ‚ÄĒ removing branches that
     were
     nearly free.
     - It pays only where branches are genuinely expensive: SIMD/GPU lane
     divergence
     (15‚Äď30√ó a predicted CPU branch) or pathological misprediction at scale
     (stream/packet processing, millions in lockstep).
     - Rule: reify control flow into data only for kernels you will place wide.
     - Note: the transition-table-as-value + parallel-scan FSM (simdjson-style)
     is
     not expressible today ‚ÄĒ scan is an unimplemented Phase-2 spec
     (tests/unit/language/collectives/scan_int.arche:2) with a fixed-monoid
     operator set (semantic.c:2496); custom-operator scan would be a real
     feature.
     Mark as such.

     4. New section "¬ß8 Control flow in leaves is banned; the monadic tail 
     decomposes"

     - Rule: generalize map's E0046 to every data-parallel leaf ‚ÄĒ control flow
     in a leaf is a hard error, unspellable, no flag and no @allow (same
     character as system-cannot-call-system). Hitting it means redesign.
     - Where control flow goes instead: pure branching/looping ‚Üí a func (it runs
     on the CPU; branches free there); conditional effects ‚Üí selective values
     (whenS/ifS); result-dependent sequencing ‚Üí decompose.
     - Worked example ‚ÄĒ the framed read (BANNED inline monadic handle ‚Üí
     branchless tick): going := (state < DONE), req := (want-have)*going,
     uniform recv, done_now := (have>=want)*going,
     want = select(done_now*was_hdr, HDR+body_len(buf), want),
     state = state + done_now; reply + evict via whenS(state==DONE, 
     send_all(...))
     and whenS(state==DONE, delete(r)) (delete IS a structural-mutation effect ‚Üí
     the selective rung gates it; deferred command buffer flushes at the
     barrier).
     - It collapses to ONE each, not separate systems. Separate systems are
     forced only by a real barrier (deferred insert/delete must land before the
     next step reads pool membership; a cross-row reduction/sort must complete;
     a
     different archetype). Decomposition spreads across ticks, not systems ‚ÄĒ
     same system count as the inline version.
     - Honest cost (cross-ref ¬ß7): on a CPU this is objectively slower ‚ÄĒ
     per-tick rescan, polling syscalls, predicated waste ‚ÄĒ and buys nothing
     there;
     right only when the FSM is placed wide.
     - Prerequisites / consequences: finish the selective layer (value-producing
     ifS, not just the wired guard form); this changes the flat-effect doc's
     ¬ß5/¬ß8 (which currently permits the inline monadic tail as an "honest cost")
     to "monadic tail = redesign trigger ‚Üí decompose"; and the csv.load
     @allow(proc_not_primitive) holdout must become the pending
     archetype-targeted
     load system, else the no-escape rule has an escape.

     5. Short note "¬ß9 The permission signature (one system, kinds as presets)"

     - One system kind carrying a permission signature: read set (the query),
     write
     set (the (mutables) list ‚ÄĒ hoisted out of the named/shared query, unlike
     Bevy's per-system &mut), and the eff flag. Kinds (map/each) are named
     flag-presets, not primitives.
     - Leaves are branchless by ban, so there is no branch flag on leaves and
     no branch color on funcs ‚ÄĒ branch-ness is just the CPU/GPU axis, derived
     whole-program in release (¬ß6), invisible in dev.

     6. Cross-references

     - Note in ¬ß5/¬ß8 that promoting these from WIP would amend
     docs/design/the-flat-effect-model.md ¬ß5/¬ß8 (currently landed law permitting
     the inline monadic tail).

     - No changes to OPEN_ITEMS.md (per user-curated-docs).

      68 +One refinement on "GPU kernel candidate," because an earlier dr
         +aft of this doc framed branch-freedom as a                     
      69 +fact *sniffed from the body*. That is the wrong framing: **bran
         +ch-freedom is not an independent property you                  
      70 +ask for ‚ÄĒ it *is* GPU-eligibility.** "Branchless" and "GPU-elig
         +ible" name the same fact. The placer derives a                 
      71 +single predicate over the unit ‚ÄĒ `branchless ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß bo
         +unded` ‚ÄĒ and that predicate *is* the CPU/GPU                   
      72 +axis: fail any conjunct and the unit is CPU-only (branches are 
         +free on a CPU anyway, ¬ß7); pass all three and                  
      73 +it is eligible for the GPU, where a cost model then decides whe
         +ther it actually goes (¬ß5, legality vs                         
      74 +profitability). So there is no "branch flag," no "explicit ask 
         +for branch power," and nothing the author                      
      75 +annotates ‚ÄĒ only a derived predicate. The author never says `@g
         +pu` and never says "branchless"; both fall                     
      76 +out of the kind they wrote and what its body touches.

‚óŹ Update(docs/wip/migration-derived-placement.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 160 lines
      209    *Profitability* ("should it?") is the static cost model. Onl
           y profitability is the genuinely-open
      210    research cell; legality is settled. So the unsolved part of 
           this doc is narrower than it first reads:
      211    not "static placement," but "static *cost* over non-affine c
           olumnar storage with no runtime scheduler."
      212 +                                                              
      213 +---                                                           
      214 +                                                              
      215 +## 6. Dev/release placement ‚ÄĒ no annotations, ever            
      216 +                                                              
      217 +The load-bearing fact that keeps placement annotation-free: **
          +placement is a performance decision, not a                    
      218 +correctness one.** A kernel computes the same result on the CP
          +U or the GPU; the CPU is always a legal home                  
      219 +for any kernel. So a placement can be *wrong* (slow) without b
          +eing *incorrect*. That decouples the two build                
      220 +modes:                                                        
      221 +                                                              
      222 +- **Dev = CPU-only.** Everything is CPU-legal, so a dev build 
          +needs **zero** placement analysis and **zero**                
      223 +  declarations ‚ÄĒ each unit compiles independently for the CPU,
          + trivially separately-compilable. The                         
      224 +  branch-freedom / GPU-eligibility question never even arises,
          + because on the CPU branches are free (¬ß7).                   
      225 +  "Approximate" placement isn't a compromise here: CPU is *exa
          +ct for results*, just unoptimized.                            
      226 +- **Release = whole-program.** GPU placement (derive `branchle
          +ss ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß bounded`, then run the cost                
      227 +  model) happens only in the optimized build, where the whole 
          +program is in hand anyway ‚ÄĒ so it is fully                    
      228 +  **derived**, never declared.                                
      229 +                                                              
      230 +This is why there are no branch/placement annotations *anywher
          +e*: dev sidesteps the question, release derives               
      231 +it whole-program. An earlier line of thought wanted to surface
          + branch-ness as a *signature color* so GPU                    
      232 +placement could be separately compiled ‚ÄĒ that idea is **cut**.
          + The only consumer of a per-unit GPU-eligibility              
      233 +bit is GPU placement, and the only mode that does GPU placemen
          +t (release) is whole-program, so the bit is                   
      234 +never needed at a module boundary.                            
      235 +                                                              
      236 +Honest flag: dev-on-CPU means GPU placement and any GPU-specif
          +ic behavior (float precision, divergence cost)                
      237 +is exercised only in release/perf builds ‚ÄĒ a normal dev/releas
          +e tradeoff (iterate logic on the CPU, validate                
      238 +placement in release), not a hidden one.                      
      239 +                                                              
      240 +## 7. Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed techniq
          +ue                                                            
      241 +                                                              
      242 +A tempting error is to read this whole document as "branches a
          +re bad, make everything branchless." On a CPU                 
      243 +that is simply false. A well-predicted branch is ~0 extra cycl
          +es; a misprediction is ~15-20; and the                        
      244 +branches in real kernels ‚ÄĒ a connection sitting in one state a
          +cross many reads, a loop bound that rarely                    
      245 +changes ‚ÄĒ are *highly* predictable. Reifying that control flow
          + into data (`select`, mask-arithmetic                         
      246 +`x * (a >= b)`, transition tables, per-tick state machines) is
          + **pure overhead on a CPU**: you pay rescans,                 
      247 +predicated wasted work, and ‚ÄĒ for I/O state machines ‚ÄĒ polling
          + syscalls, all to delete branches that cost                   
      248 +almost nothing.                                               
      249 +                                                              
      250 +Branchlessness pays *only* where branches are genuinely expens
          +ive:                                                          
      251 +                                                              
      252 +- **SIMD/GPU lane divergence** ‚ÄĒ a divergent branch masks whol
          +e lanes, 15-30√ó the cost of a predicted CPU                   
      253 +  branch. Here predication is the only way to keep lanes full.
      254 +- **Pathological misprediction at scale** ‚ÄĒ stream/packet proc
          +essing of millions of elements in lockstep,                   
      255 +  where mispredicts (not syscalls) dominate.                  
      256 +                                                              
      257 +**Rule: reify control flow into data only for the kernels you 
          +will actually place wide.** Everywhere else,                  
      258 +branches belong in funcs/systems and run on the CPU, where the
          +y are free. Branchless is the price you pay to                
      259 +make a kernel GPU-eligible and statically costable ‚ÄĒ it is not
          + a speedup you collect on the CPU.                            
      260 +                                                              
      261 +A note on one branchless idiom this doc gestured at: the *tran
          +sition-table-as-value composed by a parallel                  
      262 +scan* (the simdjson / data-parallel-FSM technique, the only wa
          +y to parallelize an inherently sequential state               
      263 +machine) is **not expressible in arche today.** `scan` is an u
          +nimplemented Phase-2 spec                                     
      264 +(`tests/unit/language/collectives/scan_int.arche:2`, "red unti
          +l scan is implemented"), and even the spec                    
      265 +restricts the scan operator to a fixed monoid set with a known
          + identity (`semantic.c:2496`) ‚ÄĒ so a                          
      266 +user-defined associative combiner (composing transition functi
          +ons) would be a real language feature                         
      267 +(custom-operator scan), not a design idiom over existing primi
          +tives. Treat the scan-FSM as future work, not                 
      268 +as something the patterns below can lean on.                  
      269 +                                                              
      270 +## 8. Control flow in leaves is banned; the monadic tail decom
          +poses                                                         
      271 +                                                              
      272 +The endpoint of "everything that touches data in parallel is b
          +ranchless" is a hard rule, with the same                      
      273 +character as the flat-effect model's *a system cannot call a s
          +ystem*: **data-dependent control flow in a leaf               
      274 +(`map`/`each`/`system`) is unspellable.** Generalize `map`'s e
          +xisting `E0046` to every leaf ‚ÄĒ a branch or a                 
      275 +data-dependent loop in a leaf body is a hard error, with **no 
          +flag and no `@allow`**. Hitting it is not a                   
      276 +case to opt out of; it is a signal to *redesign*. Control flow
          + goes to exactly three places instead:                        
      277 +                                                              
      278 +- **pure branching/looping ‚Üí a `func`** (its legitimate home ‚ÄĒ
          + recursion is free there; it runs on the CPU,                 
      279 +  where branches cost nothing);                               
      280 +- **conditional effects ‚Üí selective values** (`whenS`/`ifS`) ‚ÄĒ
          + a value the leaf runs, not an `if` in its body;              
      281 +- **result-dependent sequencing ‚Üí decompose** (state-as-data; 
          +below).                                                       
      282 +                                                              
      283 +The objection is "but the monadic tail ‚ÄĒ read a header, then r
          +ead *that many* bytes ‚ÄĒ has to live somewhere,                
      284 +and the flat-effect model puts it inline in a system/each." Th
          +e claim here is that the monadic tail is **not                
      285 +irreducible**: it decomposes, and the ban is what forces the d
          +ecomposition.                                                 
      286 +                                                              
      287 +```arche                                                      
      288 +// BEFORE ‚ÄĒ the BANNED inline monadic form (data-dependent seq
          +uencing + branches in a leaf):                                
      289 +handle :: each (query { fd, ok }) {                           
      290 +  hdr: [1]char;                                               
      291 +  read(fd, hdr, 1)(got:, err:);                               
      292 +  if err != 0 || got == 0 { ok = 0; return; }   // branch + ea
          +rly return ‚ÄĒ banned                                           
      293 +  len := int(hdr[0]);                                         
      294 +  body: [256]char;                                            
      295 +  read(fd, body, len)(got:, err:);                // read #2 S
          +HAPED BY read #1's runtime result                             
      296 +  ok = (err == 0 && got == len);                              
      297 +}                                                             
      298 +```                                                           
      299 +                                                              
      300 +```arche                                                      
      301 +// PROPOSED ‚ÄĒ state as data, one branchless step per tick. Sta
          +tes linear so "phase complete" = +1:                          
      302 +//   NEED_HDR = 0, NEED_BODY = 1, DONE = 2.   `want - have` is
          + the bytes to pull in BOTH phases                             
      303 +//   (want = HDR in phase 0, want = HDR + len in phase 1), so 
          +the read needs no state branch.                               
      304 +tick :: each (query { fd, state, want, have, buf } as r) {    
      305 +  going    := (state < DONE);              // 1 while unfinish
          +ed, else 0   (mask)                                           
      306 +  req      := (want - have) * going;       // bytes to pull; 0
          + once DONE   (mask)                                           
      307 +  recv(fd, req)(buf, got:);  have = have + got;               
      308 +  was_hdr  := (state == NEED_HDR);         // mask, BEFORE adv
          +ancing                                                        
      309 +  done_now := (have >= want) * going;      // finished this ph
          +ase this tick? (mask)                                         
      310 +  want   = select(done_now * was_hdr, HDR + body_len(buf), wan
          +t);  // re-arm `want` on header completion                    
      311 +  state  = state + done_now;               // 0->1 (hdr), 1->2
          + (body); never past DONE                                      
      312 +                                                              
      313 +  whenS(state == DONE, send_all(fd, build_response(buf, want))
          +)(_:, _:);  // reply ‚ÄĒ selective, not an `if`                 
      314 +  whenS(state == DONE, delete(r))(_:);                        
          +             // evict ‚ÄĒ `delete` IS an effect                 
      315 +}                                                             
      316 +```                                                           
      317 +                                                              
      318 +`select(c, a, b)` and mask-arithmetic are real (`tests/unit/gp
          +u/physics_step.arche:15`; README "Conditional                 
      319 +Behavior", `tests/unit/language/types/int_mask_times_float_col
          +umn.arche`). `delete` is a structural-mutation                
      320 +effect, so the selective rung gates it exactly like `send`; it
          + lowers to a guarded emit into the deferred                   
      321 +command buffer, flushed at the stage barrier (which also sides
          +teps iterator invalidation ‚ÄĒ you queue the                    
      322 +delete, the body finishes on the present row, removal happens 
          +at the seam).                                                 
      323 +                                                              
      324 +Two facts worth pinning:                                      
      325 +                                                              
      326 +- **It collapses to ONE `each`, not separate systems.** Once c
          +onditionality is `whenS`/`select` values, there               
      327 +  is nothing to *call* between the steps, so advance + reply +
          + evict are one body. Separate systems are forced              
      328 +  only by a real barrier: a deferred `insert`/`delete` must la
          +nd before the next step reads pool *membership*;              
      329 +  a cross-row reduction/sort must complete; or the next step q
          +ueries a different archetype. None hold here.                 
      330 +- **Decomposition spreads work across *ticks*, not *systems*.*
          +* The `read#1 then read#2` sequencing became                  
      331 +  `tick` re-run each loop iteration ‚ÄĒ same system count as the
          + inline version. "ECS decomposition" (a producer              
      332 +  system writes a column a consumer reads) is only forced when
          + the monadic step must be *shared between*                    
      333 +  systems or hits one of those barriers; a self-contained fram
          +ed read is just "reify state into columns + loop              
      334 +  one branchless `each`."                                     
      335 +                                                              
      336 +**Honest cost (cross-ref ¬ß7): on a CPU this is objectively slo
          +wer and buys nothing there** ‚ÄĒ per-tick rescan                
      337 +of every active connection, polling `recv`s that mostly return
          + EAGAIN, and predicated waste (`body_len` and                 
      338 +`build_response` evaluated every tick). The inline branchy eve
          +nt loop, driven by readiness (epoll), wins on a               
      339 +CPU. The branchless form is the right shape *only* if this FSM
          + is placed wide (¬ß7).                                         
      340 +                                                              
      341 +**Prerequisites / consequences.** This rule is not free to ado
          +pt:                                                           
      342 +                                                              
      343 +1. The **selective layer must be finished** ‚ÄĒ value-producing 
          +`ifS`, not just the currently-wired guard form                
      344 +   (`whenS`, `ifS` with a `pure()` else) ‚ÄĒ or legitimate stati
          +c conditionals have nowhere to land.                          
      345 +2. It **changes the flat-effect model's position.** `the-flat-
          +effect-model.md` ¬ß5/¬ß8 currently *permit* the                 
      346 +   monadic tail to live inline in a flat system/each as an "ho
          +nest cost." This rule rewrites that to "monadic               
      347 +   tail = redesign trigger ‚Üí decompose."                      
      348 +3. The one sanctioned holdout ‚ÄĒ `csv.load` under `@allow(proc_
          +not_primitive)` ‚ÄĒ must become the pending                     
      349 +   archetype-targeted load system, or the no-escape-hatch rule
          + has an escape hatch.                                         
      350 +                                                              
      351 +## 9. The permission signature (one `system`, kinds as presets
          +)                                                             
      352 +                                                              
      353 +The kinds stop being primitives. There is one `system`, carryi
          +ng a **permission signature**: the read set                   
      354 +(the query), the write set (a `(mutables)` list), and the `eff
          +` flag. The write set is a *separate list*, not               
      355 +Bevy-style `&mut` inside the query, because arche queries are 
          +**named and shared** across many systems while                
      356 +mutability is per-use ‚ÄĒ so it hoists out of the query to the s
          +ystem that writes. `map` and `each` are then                  
      357 +just named flag-presets over this signature (`map` = no `eff`,
          + fanning over a query; etc.), not distinct kinds.             
      358 +                                                              
      359 +There is deliberately **no branch flag** on this signature, an
          +d **no branch color on funcs.** Leaves are                    
      360 +branchless *by ban* (¬ß8), so they are GPU-eligible by construc
          +tion; funcs may branch freely and run on the                  
      361 +CPU. Branch-ness is not a permission to grant ‚ÄĒ it is just the
          + CPU/GPU axis (¬ß0), derived whole-program in a                
      362 +release build (¬ß6) and invisible in dev. The only signature-le
          +vel capability that gates placement is `eff`                  
      363 +(effects ‚áí CPU); branch-freedom rides along as part of the der
          +ived GPU-eligibility predicate, never as a                    
      364 +declared bit.                                                 
      365 +                                                              
      366 +---                                                           
      367 +                                                              
      368 +> **Relationship to landed law.** ¬ß6-¬ß9 are WIP. Promoting the
          +m would amend                                                 
      369 +> [the-flat-effect-model.md](../design/the-flat-effect-model.m
          +d) ¬ß5/¬ß8, which today *permits* the inline                    
      370 +> monadic tail. Until then, the flat-effect model is the sourc
          +e of truth and these sections are a proposed                  
      371 +> direction, not current behavior.

  What landed:

  - ¬ß0 ‚ÄĒ corrected the "branch-free so GPU candidate" framing: branch-freedom is
  GPU-eligibility (the derived predicate branchless ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß bounded),

  derived predicate; only the static cost model is the open research cell.
  Narrows what ¬ß5 calls unsolved.
  - ¬ß6 Dev/release placement ‚ÄĒ placement is performance not correctness ‚áí dev =
  CPU-only (trivially separately-compilable, zero declarations), release =
  whole-program derived GPU placement. The signature-color-for-sep-comp idea is
  explicitly cut, with the honest dev/release flag.
  - ¬ß7 Branchless is a placement technique, not a speed technique ‚ÄĒ CPU branch
  predictor makes branches ~free; reification is overhead unless placed wide;

  spec, fixed-monoid operators only).
  - ¬ß8 Control flow in leaves is banned ‚ÄĒ hard/unspellable, no flag, no @allow;
  the BANNED inline handle ‚Üí branchless tick worked example (verified
  select/mask/whenS/deferred-delete); collapses to one each, not separate

  are presets; no branch flag, no func branch-color ‚ÄĒ branch-ness is just the

  Checksums identical (2.1347e8, ‚Č† initial 2e7) ‚ÄĒ both kinds compute the same
  thing and the passes really ran. each is consistently ~5‚Äď10% slower than map 
  for identical pure column work on the CPU, order-independent.

  What it means

  This nuances the WIP doc's ¬ß7/¬ß9 claim that "the kind is a placement preset,
  not a CPU speed difference." There is a small, real CPU cost ‚ÄĒ almost
  certainly because each (the effect-capable leaf) emits per-row bookkeeping a
  map omits (row handles, deleted-row skipping, command-buffer setup), even when
  the body runs no effects. It's ~8%, not nothing. So the honest statement is
  "kind is mostly a placement preset; each carries a modest per-row overhead a
  pure map avoids" ‚ÄĒ which is itself an argument for the ¬ß9 framing (a pure
  column kernel should be the no-eff preset, i.e. map, precisely so it sheds
  that overhead).

  Two notes

  - I had to rebuild the compiler. The committed build/arche (root-owned,
  Jun¬†26) was stale and failed on the repo's own examples (#import { fmt }
  unrecognized). I removed the stale root-owned build artifacts in build/
  (regenerable outputs only) and did an incremental rebuild ‚Üí build/arche is now
  current (0.4.37-dev, curt-owned).
  - Likely compiler false-positive: unused_function fires on the
  laps_map/laps_each Schedule-combinator funcs even though they're folded into
  #run (the passes demonstrably ran). The unused_function lint doesn't seem to
  count schedule-fold usage. I did not @allow-suppress it (per your honest-red
  ethos) ‚ÄĒ flagging it as a probable lint blind spot worth a regression test.

  Want me to (a) dig into the codegen to pin down why each is +8% (confirm it's
  row bookkeeping), (b) add a third arm ‚ÄĒ a scalar system with a hand-indexed
  for loop (the --pool-index=allow form) ‚ÄĒ for a map/each/manual-loop
  comparison, or (c) fold the ¬ß7/¬ß9 nuance ("each ‚Čą +8% vs map on CPU") into the
  WIP doc?

  comparison; map-on-GPU is the one that actually tests the ¬ß7 thesis. Let me
  find how GPU placement is triggered today.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ @gpu is very much a thing in the current compiler ‚ÄĒ it's a decorator on a map,
  with two build flags: --emit-gpu <dir> (emit the GLSL compute shader, CPU
  build unchanged) and --gpu (actually dispatch @gpu maps on the GPU at runtime,
  CPU fallback if no device). Note it only applies to map ‚ÄĒ never each/system,
  exactly the GPU-eligibility split we've been discussing. Let me check whether
  this box even has a GPU, and prove the map emits a shader.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

  actually testable. Let me confirm --gpu works end-to-end and whether I can
  tell it ran on the device vs fell back to CPU.

  the runtime comment says buffers are created+freed per dispatch with no

‚óŹ The bug is localized to codegen.c:9654‚Äď9660: the dispatch path builds the name
  global via emit_string_global(ctx, "\"step\"") but then GEPs it as [strlen+1 
  x i8] (= [5 x i8] for "step"), and the referenced global is never defined in

  Read 1 file, ran 2 shell commands (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ @gpu is real and current. Here's the full picture from poking the actual
  compiler:

  What @gpu is today
  - A decorator on a map only (never each/system ‚ÄĒ the GPU-eligibility split
  we've been discussing, enforced in the compiler).
  - --emit-gpu <dir>: emits a GLSL compute shader per @gpu map (CPU build
  unchanged). This works ‚ÄĒ step lowered to a clean layout(local_size_x=64)
  compute shader, and the select became a GLSL ternary. So the branchless map is
  genuinely GPU-portable ‚ÄĒ the ¬ß7 payoff, demonstrated.
  - --gpu: embeds SPIR-V and dispatches on the GPU at runtime (CPU fallback if
  no device). There's a real device here (NVIDIA GTX 1650 + glslc 2026.2).

  But --gpu is currently broken
  The runtime-dispatch build fails at IR optimization for every @gpu map
  (confirmed with a minimal no-fmt repro; the same files build+run fine on CPU):
  opt: error: use of undefined value '@.str.5fbb71b6...'   ( [5 x i8] = "step\0"
  )
  Root cause located: codegen.c:9656 builds the kernel-name string for
  arche_gpu_dispatch(name,‚Ä¶) via emit_string_global ‚Üí intern_global (which
  appends the definition to globals_buffer), but on the dispatch path that
  definition never reaches the module ‚ÄĒ so the IR references @.str.<hash> with
  no definition. A globals-emission/flush bug specific to the --gpu dispatch
  codegen. (make test-gpu only validates emitted shaders via glslc/spirv-val ‚ÄĒ
  it never exercises runtime dispatch, which is why this slipped.)

  Two caveats even once it builds
  - The runtime "creates+frees buffers per dispatch, host-visible mapped, no
  staging copy; persistent residency is future" (its own comment). So a 30-pass
  GPU benchmark would be transfer/setup-bound, not compute-bound ‚ÄĒ exactly the
  GPU-residency-across-frames that migration ¬ß2 marks as unbuilt. A fair GPU
  number needs one-dispatch-per-frame framing, stated explicitly.
  - Design-wise, @gpu is the bootstrap manual trigger; the WIP doc (¬ß5/¬ß6) wants
  placement derived and @gpu gone. So it existing now isn't a contradiction ‚ÄĒ
  it's the current scaffold for the not-yet-built derived placement.

  Where that leaves the benchmark: the CPU map vs each arm is solid (each ~+8%).
  The GPU arm ‚ÄĒ the one that actually tests "branchless map pays off wide" ‚ÄĒ is
  blocked on that --gpu codegen bug.

  Want me to fix the --gpu name-string emission bug (small, localized; + a
  regression test per your every-bug rule, since test-gpu clearly doesn't cover
  dispatch), then add the GPU arm to the benchmark (framed honestly around the
  per-dispatch / no-residency reality)? Or leave GPU as a documented blocker and
  keep the CPU comparison?

  The hand-written system loop is ~2.4√ó faster than the map. This is the
  opposite of what the WIP doc ¬ß7 ("kind is a placement preset, not a CPU speed
  difference") and this benchmark's own header comment ("map should be at least
  as fast") claimed. Both are empirically refuted: on the CPU the recommended
  idiom (map) is 2.4√ó behind hand code, and each is slowest.

  What the asm shows (honest, partial):
  - step_map is a vectorized out-of-line function (packed ...ps ops present)
  called 30√ó.
  - step_each is inlined per pass with explicit per-row loops (eachrow_body_2.i,
  30 unrolled copies) ‚ÄĒ code bloat + the +9% over map.
  - The hand-loop system is the fastest despite touching the same SoA column
  layout.

  So step_map does vectorize, yet still loses 2.4√ó to the hand loop ‚ÄĒ meaning
  the gap isn't "map doesn't SIMD," it's something structural in the map's
  per-dispatch/iteration lowering (call overhead, strided/gather access, or
  bounds setup). I haven't pinned the exact cause ‚ÄĒ that needs real IR/asm
  tracing, not grep counts, and I won't guess.

  And the GPU arm ‚ÄĒ the one where the map is supposed to win ‚ÄĒ is still blocked
  by the --gpu name-string codegen bug. So right now: map is the slowest-but-one
  on CPU and unavailable on GPU. That's a pointed finding about the current
  state.

  The benchmark file
  (design_analysis/benchmarks/systems/arche/map_vs_each_step.arche) now has all
  three arms and is committed-ready.

  Next, pick any:
  - (a) trace why the vectorized map loses 2.4√ó to a hand loop (emit --emit 
  llvm-ir, compare the loop structure properly);
  - (b) fix the --gpu codegen bug + regression test, then add the GPU arm (the
  map's actual payoff);
  - (c) correct ¬ß7 in the WIP doc with this measured reality (map is not free on
  CPU ‚ÄĒ it's 2.4√ó behind hand code today);
  - (d) leave it here.

  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  map and the whole-column system are identical (~170ms). This validates ¬ß7/¬ß9 ‚ÄĒ
  for whole-column work the kind is just a placement preset, no CPU speed
  difference. each is the only outlier (~12% slower ‚ÄĒ the per-row-fan overhead
  the asm showed as inlined eachrow_body loops).

  So retract last turn's "system is 2.4√ó faster, ¬ß7 refuted" ‚ÄĒ that was my 
  error. It came from the for-loop arm you told me to drop, and the reason it
  was faster is the genuinely interesting part:

  - Whole-column ops are unfused. Each statement (MoverC.cx = ‚Ä¶, MoverC.cvx = ‚Ä¶,
  ‚Ä¶) is a separate full-column pass ‚ÄĒ 6 sweeps over 2M elements, so the kernel
  is memory-bandwidth-bound on 6√ó the traffic.
  - The hand for loop fused all 6 ops into one pass per element ‚ÄĒ data stays in
  registers across the 6 ops, 1 sweep instead of 6 ‚Üí ~2.4√ó faster.

  That 2.4√ó gap is orthogonal to the kind (map and system suffer it equally) ‚ÄĒ
  it's the cost of no cross-statement fusion in the whole-column lowering. Which
  lines up with the project's own state (fusion was cut from the ParOp work).
  My earlier write-up wrongly pinned it on the map kind; it's really fusion, and
  it hits map and system the same.

  So the honest, corrected conclusions:
  1. Kind is a placement preset on CPU (map ‚Čą system, whole-column) ‚ÄĒ ¬ß7/¬ß9
  stands, not refuted.
  2. each carries ~12% per-row-fan overhead vs whole-column map/system.
  3. Unfused whole-column ops cost ~2.4√ó vs a fused loop ‚ÄĒ a real,
  kind-independent gap (cut fusion), separate from the placement question.

  The benchmark file now uses whole-column ops for all three arms. Want me to
  (a) add a clearly-labeled fused baseline arm to quantify the fusion gap
  properly (without calling it "the system version"), (b) note finding #3
  (fusion cost) in the WIP doc, and/or (c) still pursue the --gpu fix for the
  GPU arm?
