  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Fourth arm added and confirmed (identical checksums, stable). perf isn't
  available in this sandbox, but I don't need it ‚ÄĒ the timings themselves match
  a pure memory-bandwidth model almost exactly, which is the explanation.

  Why the vectorized column ops are 2.4√ó slower than the vectorized for-loop

  Because both are equally vectorized ‚ÄĒ and vectorization is irrelevant here. 
  The kernel is memory-bandwidth-bound, and the whole-column form moves ~2√ó the 
  bytes.

  A whole-column op is one implicit loop per statement. The step has 6
  statements, so map and the whole-column system each do 6 separate full sweeps
  over the 2M-row columns. A 2M-float column is 8 MB ‚ÄĒ far bigger than L2/L3 ‚ÄĒ
  so nothing survives in cache between sweeps: every statement re-streams its
  operands from RAM and writes its result back to RAM.

  Count the traffic per pass (each column stream = 8 MB):

  whole-column (6 separate loops):
    cvx=cvx-(cx-k)*k   R cvx, R cx,  W cvx
    cvy=cvy-(cy-k)*k   R cvy, R cy,  W cvy
    cvx*=0.99          R cvx,        W cvx
    cvy*=0.99          R cvy,        W cvy
    cx+=cvx            R cx, R cvx,  W cx
    cy+=cvy            R cy, R cvy,  W cy
    ‚Üí 10 reads + 6 writes = 16 √ó 8 MB ‚Čą 128 MB / pass

  fused for-loop (1 loop):
    load dx,dy,dvx,dvy once ‚Üí all 6 ops in registers ‚Üí store dx,dy,dvx,dvy
    ‚Üí 4 reads + 4 writes = 8 √ó 8 MB ‚Čą 64 MB / pass   (intermediates never touch
  RAM)

  Now check it against the clock ‚ÄĒ 30 passes, at a typical desktop streaming
  bandwidth of ~22 GB/s:

  - unfused: 128 MB √ó 30 = 3.84 GB √∑ 22 GB/s ‚Čą 175 ms ‚Üí measured ~178 ms ‚úď
  - fused: 64 MB √ó 30 = 1.92 GB √∑ ~26 GB/s ‚Čą 74 ms ‚Üí measured ~73 ms ‚úď

  The measured times are the memory-traffic prediction. The compute is ~10
  flops/element (~0.1 ns/element with SIMD); moving 64 bytes/element from RAM is
  ~2‚Äď3 ns/element ‚ÄĒ memory is ~20√ó the bottleneck. So:

  - SIMD speeds up the flops, but flops aren't the bottleneck ‚ÄĒ bytes moved are.
  That's why "explicitly lowered to vectorized ops" doesn't make the column
  form fast: you can't vectorize your way out of a bandwidth wall.
  - The fused loop wins purely by keeping intermediates (dvx, dvy) in registers 
  across the 6 ops, so they never round-trip to RAM ‚Üí half the traffic ‚Üí ~2√ó the
  speed. Same SIMD, half the bytes.

  This is loop/kernel fusion, and it's orthogonal to both vectorization and the
  kind:
  - map ‚Čą whole-column system (~178 vs ~181 ms) ‚ÄĒ both unfused, both pay the
  full bandwidth tax ‚Üí confirms kind is a placement preset.
  - each is +7% on top (per-row-fan bookkeeping).
  - the fused loop escapes the tax ‚ÄĒ the only one that does.

  And it lines up with the project's own state: fusion was cut from the ParOp 
  work. This benchmark quantifies that cut ‚ÄĒ for a 6-statement column kernel
  it's ~2.4√ó on a bandwidth-bound workload. Closing it means fusing adjacent
  whole-column/map statements into one pass so intermediates stay in registers
  (classic loop fusion / a fused ParOp pipeline).

  So the honest one-liner: arche's column/map model vectorizes fine but is 
  unfused, so multi-statement kernels are memory-bandwidth-bound at ~2√ó off 
  hand-fused code ‚ÄĒ and SIMD can't help because the wall is bytes, not flops.

  Want me to (a) note this fusion finding (with the bandwidth model) in the WIP
  doc, (b) commit the 4-arm benchmark, or (c) move on to the --gpu fix?

‚úĽ Worked for 3m 20s

‚ĚĮ well we need to listen to the data. Compile time abstractions should not lose 
  speed                                                                         

‚óŹ Agreed ‚ÄĒ that's the zero-cost-abstraction principle, and the data says it's
  being violated. But there's a sharper question hiding here that I should pin
  down first: the map body is semantically a single per-element pass (avx=‚Ä¶; 
  avy=‚Ä¶; ‚Ä¶; ax=ax+avx) ‚ÄĒ it should lower to exactly the fused for-loop, one
  sweep with intermediates in registers. Yet it measured the same as the unfused
  whole-column system (~178 vs ~181), not the fused loop (~73). That means the
  map itself is likely being lowered as 6 separate column passes instead of one
  fused per-element loop. Let me verify before proposing a fix.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Confirmed ‚ÄĒ and it's worse than "unfused statements": the map itself is the 
  problem. The IR proves it. A single step_map kernel with 6 statements lowers
  to six separate vectorized loops (vec_loop_8, vec_loop_41, vec_loop_74,
  vec_loop_99, vec_loop_124, ‚Ä¶) ‚ÄĒ one full-column loop per statement, each
  streaming the columns from RAM again:

  vec_loop_8   ‚Üí avx = avx - (ax-400)*0.05    (loop 1, full column)
  vec_loop_41  ‚Üí avy = avy - (ay-300)*0.05    (loop 2, full column)
  vec_loop_74  ‚Üí avx = avx * 0.99             (loop 3, full column)
  ... 3 more ...

  So a map body is not compiled as one per-element kernel (load row ‚Üí do all 6
  ops in registers ‚Üí store row, like the hand for-loop). It's compiled as a
  sequence of independent whole-column ops ‚ÄĒ 6 memory sweeps. That's exactly why
  map ‚Čą whole-column system ‚Čą 2.4√ó slower than the for-loop: the map 
  abstraction doesn't fuse its own body. This is the zero-cost violation,
  located precisely.

  You're right that this shouldn't stand. The fix is intra-kernel statement 
  fusion: a map/each body (and a whole-column system) should emit one loop whose
  body runs all statements per element, intermediates staying in registers ‚ÄĒ
  making map compile to exactly the for-loop and erasing the 2.4√ó. Let me scope
  where that lives in codegen before proposing how.

  ‚Ēā each           ‚Ēā per-row pass) ‚Ēā per-row        ‚Ēā ~190 ‚Ēā overhead      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā               ‚Ēā overhead)      ‚Ēā      ‚Ēā               ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā hand for-loop  ‚Ēā yes           ‚Ēā yes            ‚Ēā ~73  ‚Ēā neither ‚ÄĒ     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā               ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā      ‚Ēā optimal       ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The codegen path proves it: in a map/whole-column-system body, each col = expr
  statement is lowered independently ‚ÄĒ emit_map_op ‚Üí emit_whole_column_loop
  (codegen.c:8954, 2796, 6594), one loop per statement. So step_map's 6
  statements = 6 separate vectorized column loops (vec_loop_8/41/74/99/124/‚Ä¶).
  each (codegen.c:11438) is the opposite ‚ÄĒ one fused per-row loop, but scalar
  with fan overhead.

  So neither abstraction gets both fusion and vectorization; the hand loop gets 
  both. That's the zero-cost violation, exactly. The map should lower to the
  for-loop and is 2.4√ó off because it splits its own body into per-column
  passes.

  The fix

  Fuse a kernel body's consecutive whole-column assignments into one vectorized 
  per-element loop ‚ÄĒ load each row's inputs once, compute all statements' RHS in
  registers (intermediates as SSA values, not column write-backs), store the
  results. That is the hand for-loop, and it's provably safe: a map body is
  per-element-independent (no cross-row deps), so collapsing N whole-column
  passes into one per-element pass preserves semantics.

  - Where: the map-body statement loop (codegen.c ~8954) currently calls
  emit_map_op per assignment. Instead, batch a run of compatible Map ParOps over
  the same archetype/count and emit a single fused loop (extend
  emit_whole_column_loop / cpu_emit_map to take multiple (col, rhs) pairs).
  - Payoff: map ‚Üí ~73ms (matches the for-loop), 2.4√ó faster, abstraction becomes
  zero-cost. (each's scalar/overhead path is a separate, second fix.)
  - Regression test (per your every-bug rule): an IR test asserting a
  multi-statement map body emits one loop, plus the benchmark as the perf guard
  (map_ms ‚Čą loop_ms).

  This is a real codegen change to the core ‚ÄĒ well-scoped and safe, but not a
  one-liner. Want me to implement the map-body fusion now (with the regression
  test), or write it up as a plan first?

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 1m 5s

     ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
     ‚Ēā hand fused        ‚Ēā ~73  ‚Ēā 1 vectorized pass, intermediates in          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for-loop          ‚Ēā      ‚Ēā registers                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

     IR proof: a single step_map body of 6 statements lowers to
     vec_loop_8/41/74/99/124/‚Ä¶ ‚ÄĒ one
     full-column loop per statement. Each sweep re-streams its columns from RAM
     (an 8 MB column ‚Čę cache),
     so the kernel is memory-bandwidth-bound: ~128 MB/pass vs the fused loop's
     ~64 MB/pass. The measured
     times match a ~22 GB/s bandwidth model exactly (3.84 GB √∑ 22 ‚Čą 175 ms; 1.92
     GB √∑ 26 ‚Čą 74 ms).

     So the map abstraction is not zero-cost ‚ÄĒ it's 2.4√ó slower than the obvious
     hand loop, purely
     because it splits its own per-element body into per-statement column
     passes. The principle: a compile-time
     abstraction must not lose speed. Fix = fuse a kernel body's consecutive 
     column assignments into one
     per-element loop, so map compiles to exactly the hand loop. This is
     provably safe: a map body is
     per-row-independent, and statements stay in source order at the shared
     index, so an intra-body
     read-after-write on a column (ax = ax + avx after avx = ‚Ä¶) reads the
     just-stored value.

     Scope

     In-scope: the map and whole-column system lowering (the emit_map_op /
     emit_whole_column_loop paths). Out-of-scope (separate follow-up, note
     only): the each per-row fan's
     scalar/overhead path (it's already fused but not vectorized) and any
     cross-kernel/schedule fusion.

     Approach (all in codegen/codegen.c)

     1. A fused multi-store loop emitter

     Add emit_fused_column_loop(ctx, items[], n, count, struct_ptr) modeled on
     emit_whole_column_loop
     (codegen.c:6594). Each item carries { col_ptr, rhs, op, scalar_type, 
     arche_type } (the current
     emit_map_op args, codegen.c:2838). It emits one
     vec_loop+scalar_setup+scalar_body+done
     structure (reuse the existing label/scheme at 6624‚Äď6631), and in the body,
     in source order:
     - hoist every item's column-base GEP once (hoist_column_geps,¬†6602) before
     the loop;
     - set ctx->implicit_loop_index = vi once; share it across all items;
     - for each item: evaluate rhs via codegen_expression at vi, apply the
     compound op if any (reuse the
     load+op+store block at 6659‚Äď6705), and store to its column at vi.
     Vectorize the whole group (set ctx->vector_lanes = 4) only if every item is
     float and none is
     rhs_forces_scalar (6649); otherwise emit the group scalar (still one fused
     pass ‚ÄĒ fusion helps even
     unvectorized). The scalar tail mirrors the vector body for the count & 3
     remainder.

     2. Group consecutive assignments at the map-body lowering site

     At the statement walk that currently calls emit_map_op per assignment
     (codegen.c:8954 for the
     map-parameter "Path B", and the HIR_EXPR_FIELD "Path A" sibling at ~8958+;
     also the whole-column-system
     paths ~9029/9129/9161), replace per-statement emission with: scan forward a
     maximal run of statements
     that are all column assignments over the same archetype + same count, with
     no intervening
     non-assignment statement and a consistent vectorization class, collect
     their item descriptors, and emit
     the run via emit_fused_column_loop. A run of length 1 reproduces today's
     behavior (can still go through
     the fused emitter). Split a run at: a different archetype, a non-assignment
     statement, or a
     vectorize/scalar class change (so a scalar-forcing item starts a new
     group).

     3. Keep one code path

     Route emit_map_op (the existing single-statement helper, 4 call sites)
     through emit_fused_column_loop
     with n=1, so there is a single loop-emitter and the grouping is the only
     new control flow.

     Critical files

     - codegen/codegen.c ‚ÄĒ new emit_fused_column_loop; grouping logic at the
     map/each-body statement walk
     (~8954 and sibling paths); reuse emit_whole_column_loop internals (6594),
     hoist_column_geps (6487),
     rhs_forces_scalar (6649), emit_int_divmod, float_promote_operand.
     - design_analysis/benchmarks/systems/arche/map_vs_each_step.arche ‚ÄĒ the
     perf guard (already written).

     Verification

     - Correctness: make test (or the map/each/system + collectives suites); the
     benchmark checksums must
     stay 2.1347e+08 for all arms. Spot-check intra-body read-after-write
     kernels
     (tests/unit/language/systems/soa_array_only.arche, the tuple_* tests at
     tests/unit/language/tuples/) still produce identical output.
     - IR: build the benchmark with --emit llvm-ir; assert step_map's function
     body now contains one
     vec_loop_* (was six). Add a small regression test (arche file + IR/stdout
     assertion) per the
     every-bug rule, since no existing test covers loop-count/fusion.
     - Perf: rebuild and run the 4-arm benchmark; map_ms should drop from ~178
     to ‚Čą loop_ms (~73),
     i.e. within ~20% of the hand loop, and whole-column sys_ms likewise.
     - Build the compiler with make -j build/arche (note: the committed binary
     was stale; current tree builds
     clean to 0.4.37-dev).

     Out of scope / follow-ups (noted, not done here)

     - each per-row fan: fused but scalar ‚ÄĒ vectorizing it is a separate change.
     - --gpu runtime dispatch is currently broken (undefined name-string global,
     codegen.c:9656) ‚ÄĒ unrelated
     bug, tracked separately.

           +_lanes (0 = scalar, 4 = AVX). Shared by the                  
      6627 + * fused multi-statement loop (flush_map_batch); mirrors the 
           +per-statement body of emit_whole_column_loop. */             
      6628 +static void emit_column_assign_body(CodegenContext *ctx, cons
           +t char *col_ptr, const char *scalar_type,                    
      6629 +                                    const char *arche_type, H
           +irExpr *rhs, int op, const char *idx) {                      
      6630 +  int col_is_float = strcmp(arche_type, "float") == 0 || strc
           +mp(arche_type, "double") == 0;                               
      6631 +  int col_unsigned = arche_type[0] == 'u';                   
      6632 +  int vec = ctx->vector_lanes > 0;                           
      6633 +                                                             
      6634 +  char rhs_buf[256];                                         
      6635 +  codegen_expression(ctx, rhs, rhs_buf);                     
      6636 +                                                             
      6637 +  char compute_result[256];                                  
      6638 +  strcpy(compute_result, rhs_buf);                           
      6639 +  if (op != OP_NONE) {                                       
      6640 +    char *loaded = gen_value_name(ctx);                      
      6641 +    char *gep = gen_value_name(ctx);                         
      6642 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = getelementptr %s, %s* %s, 
           +i64 %s\n", gep, scalar_type, scalar_type, col_ptr, idx);     
      6643 +    const char *load_type = vec ? elem_llvm_type(ctx, arche_t
           +ype) : scalar_type;                                          
      6644 +    const char *load_src = gep;                              
      6645 +    if (vec) {                                               
      6646 +      char *vec_ptr = gen_value_name(ctx);                   
      6647 +      buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = bitcast %s* %s to %s*\n"
           +, vec_ptr, scalar_type, gep, load_type);                     
      6648 +      load_src = vec_ptr;                                    
      6649 +    }                                                        
      6650 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = load %s, %s* %s, align %d\
           +n", loaded, load_type, load_type, load_src, vec ? 8 : 4);    
      6651 +    const char *op_str;                                      
      6652 +    switch (op) {                                            
      6653 +    case OP_ADD:                                             
      6654 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "fadd" : "add";                
      6655 +      break;                                                 
      6656 +    case OP_SUB:                                             
      6657 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "fsub" : "sub";                
      6658 +      break;                                                 
      6659 +    case OP_MUL:                                             
      6660 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "fmul" : "mul";                
      6661 +      break;                                                 
      6662 +    case OP_DIV:                                             
      6663 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "fdiv" : (col_unsigned ? "udiv"
           + : "sdiv");                                                  
      6664 +      break;                                                 
      6665 +    case OP_MOD:                                             
      6666 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "frem" : (col_unsigned ? "urem"
           + : "srem");                                                  
      6667 +      break;                                                 
      6668 +    default:                                                 
      6669 +      op_str = col_is_float ? "fadd" : "add";                
      6670 +      break;                                                 
      6671 +    }                                                        
      6672 +    char *op_result = gen_value_name(ctx);                   
      6673 +    char rhs_promo[256];                                     
      6674 +    const char *rhs_op =                                     
      6675 +        col_is_float ? float_promote_operand(ctx, rhs, rhs_bu
           +f, rhs_promo, sizeof(rhs_promo)) : rhs_buf;                  
      6676 +    if (!col_is_float && (op == OP_DIV || op == OP_MOD))     
      6677 +      emit_int_divmod(ctx, op_str, load_type, loaded, rhs_buf
           +, NULL, op_result);                                          
      6678 +    else                                                     
      6679 +      buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = %s %s %s, %s\n", op_resu
           +lt, op_str, load_type, loaded, rhs_op);                      
      6680 +    strcpy(compute_result, op_result);                       
      6681 +  }                                                          
      6682 +                                                             
      6683 +  char *target_gep = gen_value_name(ctx);                    
      6684 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = getelementptr %s, %s* %s, i6
           +4 %s\n", target_gep, scalar_type, scalar_type, col_ptr,      
      6685 +                    idx);                                    
      6686 +  if (op == OP_NONE && scalar_type[0] == 'i') {              
      6687 +    char coerced[256];                                       
      6688 +    emit_int_convert(ctx, compute_result, &rhs->resolved, ato
           +i(scalar_type + 1), coerced);                                
      6689 +    strcpy(compute_result, coerced);                         
      6690 +  }                                                          
      6691 +  if (vec) {                                                 
      6692 +    const char *vec_type = elem_llvm_type(ctx, arche_type);  
      6693 +    char *vec_ptr = gen_value_name(ctx);                     
      6694 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = bitcast %s* %s to %s*\n", 
           +vec_ptr, scalar_type, target_gep, vec_type);                 
      6695 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store %s %s, %s* %s, align 8\n"
           +, vec_type, compute_result, vec_type, vec_ptr);              
      6696 +  } else {                                                   
      6697 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store %s %s, %s* %s, align 4\n"
           +, scalar_type, compute_result, scalar_type, target_gep);     
      6698 +  }                                                          
      6699 +}                                                            
      6700 +                                                             
      6701 +/* Emit ONE fused loop running every recorded column assignme
           +nt per element (intermediates stay in                        
      6702 + * registers) ‚ÄĒ the zero-cost-abstraction fix: a multi-statem
           +ent map/whole-column body compiles to a                      
      6703 + * single pass over the rows instead of one full-column sweep
           + per statement. */                                           
      6704 +static void flush_map_batch(CodegenContext *ctx) {           
      6705 +  int n = ctx->map_batch_count;                              
      6706 +  if (n <= 0) {                                              
      6707 +    ctx->map_batch_count = 0;                                
      6708 +    return;                                                  
      6709 +  }                                                          
      6710 +  MapBatchItem *items = ctx->map_batch_items;                
      6711 +  const char *count = items[0].count; /* same archetype ‚áí sam
           +e count for every item */                                    
      6712 +                                                             
      6713 +  /* Vectorize the whole group only if EVERY item is a float 
           +column with no scalar-forcing RHS. */                        
      6714 +  int vectorize = 1;                                         
      6715 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {                              
      6716 +    const char *at = items[i].arche_type;                    
      6717 +    int is_f = strcmp(at, "float") == 0 || strcmp(at, "double
           +") == 0;                                                     
      6718 +    if (!is_f || rhs_forces_scalar(ctx, items[i].rhs)) {     
      6719 +      vectorize = 0;                                         
      6720 +      break;                                                 
      6721 +    }                                                        
      6722 +  }                                                          
      6723 +                                                             
      6724 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)                                
      6725 +    if (items[i].struct_ptr)                                 
      6726 +      hoist_column_geps(ctx, items[i].rhs, items[i].struct_pt
           +r);                                                          
      6727 +                                                             
      6728 +  char *count_aligned = gen_value_name(ctx);                 
      6729 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = and i64 %s, -4\n", count_ali
           +gned, count);                                                
      6730 +                                                             
      6731 +  char *v_ctr_alloca = gen_value_name(ctx);                  
      6732 +  emit_alloca(ctx, "  %s = alloca i64\n", v_ctr_alloca);     
      6733 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store i64 0, i64* %s\n", v_ctr_al
           +loca);                                                       
      6734 +                                                             
      6735 +  char vloop[40], vbody[40], ssetup[40], scheck[40], sbody[40
           +], done[40];                                                 
      6736 +  snprintf(vloop, sizeof(vloop), "fmap_vloop_%d", ctx->value_
           +counter++);                                                  
      6737 +  snprintf(vbody, sizeof(vbody), "fmap_vbody_%d", ctx->value_
           +counter++);                                                  
      6738 +  snprintf(ssetup, sizeof(ssetup), "fmap_ssetup_%d", ctx->val
           +ue_counter++);                                               
      6739 +  snprintf(scheck, sizeof(scheck), "fmap_scheck_%d", ctx->val
           +ue_counter++);                                               
      6740 +  snprintf(sbody, sizeof(sbody), "fmap_sbody_%d", ctx->value_
           +counter++);                                                  
      6741 +  snprintf(done, sizeof(done), "fmap_done_%d", ctx->value_cou
           +nter++);                                                     
      6742 +                                                             
      6743 +  /* Vector (or unit-stride scalar) loop over the aligned pre
           +fix. */                                                      
      6744 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br label %%%s\n\n%s:\n", vloop, v
           +loop);                                                       
      6745 +  char *vi = gen_value_name(ctx);                            
      6746 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = load i64, i64* %s\n", vi, v_
           +ctr_alloca);                                                 
      6747 +  char *vcond = gen_value_name(ctx);                         
      6748 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = icmp slt i64 %s, %s\n", vcon
           +d, vi, count_aligned);                                       
      6749 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br i1 %s, label %%%s, label %%%s\
           +n\n%s:\n", vcond, vbody, ssetup, vbody);                     
      6750 +  ctx->vector_lanes = vectorize ? 4 : 0;                     
      6751 +  snprintf(ctx->implicit_loop_index, sizeof(ctx->implicit_loo
           +p_index), "%s", vi);                                         
      6752 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)                                
      6753 +    emit_column_assign_body(ctx, items[i].col_ptr, items[i].s
           +calar_type, items[i].arche_type, items[i].rhs,               
      6754 +                            items[i].op, vi);                
      6755 +  char *vi_new = gen_value_name(ctx);                        
      6756 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = add i64 %s, %d\n", vi_new, v
           +i, vectorize ? 4 : 1);                                       
      6757 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store i64 %s, i64* %s\n", vi_new,
           + v_ctr_alloca);                                              
      6758 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br label %%%s\n\n", vloop);      
      6759 +                                                             
      6760 +  /* Scalar tail over the remaining `count & 3` elements. */ 
      6761 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "%s:\n", ssetup);                   
      6762 +  char *s_ctr_alloca = gen_value_name(ctx);                  
      6763 +  emit_alloca(ctx, "  %s = alloca i64\n", s_ctr_alloca);     
      6764 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store i64 %s, i64* %s\n", count_a
           +ligned, s_ctr_alloca);                                       
      6765 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br label %%%s\n\n%s:\n", scheck, 
           +scheck);                                                     
      6766 +  char *si = gen_value_name(ctx);                            
      6767 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = load i64, i64* %s\n", si, s_
           +ctr_alloca);                                                 
      6768 +  char *scond = gen_value_name(ctx);                         
      6769 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = icmp slt i64 %s, %s\n", scon
           +d, si, count);                                               
      6770 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br i1 %s, label %%%s, label %%%s\
           +n\n%s:\n", scond, sbody, done, sbody);                       
      6771 +  ctx->vector_lanes = 0;                                     
      6772 +  snprintf(ctx->implicit_loop_index, sizeof(ctx->implicit_loo
           +p_index), "%s", si);                                         
      6773 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)                                
      6774 +    emit_column_assign_body(ctx, items[i].col_ptr, items[i].s
           +calar_type, items[i].arche_type, items[i].rhs,               
      6775 +                            items[i].op, si);                
      6776 +  char *si_new = gen_value_name(ctx);                        
      6777 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = add i64 %s, 1\n", si_new, si
           +);                                                           
      6778 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  store i64 %s, i64* %s\n", si_new,
           + s_ctr_alloca);                                              
      6779 +  buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  br label %%%s\n\n%s:\n", scheck, 
           +done);                                                       
      6780 +                                                             
      6781 +  ctx->implicit_loop_index[0] = '\0';                        
      6782 +  ctx->vector_lanes = 0;                                     
      6783 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {                              
      6784 +    free(items[i].col_ptr);                                  
      6785 +    free(items[i].count);                                    
      6786 +    free(items[i].scalar_type);                              
      6787 +    free(items[i].arche_type);                               
      6788 +    free(items[i].struct_ptr);                               
      6789 +  }                                                          
      6790 +  ctx->map_batch_count = 0;                                  
      6791 +}                                                            
      6792 +                                                             
      6793 +/* True if a body statement is a whole-column assignment (Pat
           +h A field-column or Path B map-param column) ‚ÄĒ               
      6794 + * the statements that funnel through emit_whole_column_loop 
           +and are therefore fusable. */                                
      6795 +static int stmt_targets_column(CodegenContext *ctx, HirStmt *
           +stmt) {                                                      
      6796 +  if (stmt->kind != HIR_STMT_ASSIGN)                         
      6797 +    return 0;                                                
      6798 +  HirExpr *t = stmt->data.assign_stmt.target;                
      6799 +  if (t->kind == HIR_EXPR_FIELD)                             
      6800 +    return 1;                                                
      6801 +  if (t->kind == HIR_EXPR_NAME) {                            
      6802 +    ValueInfo *v = find_value(ctx, t->data.name.name);       
      6803 +    return v && v->type == 4; /* type 4 = column pointer (map
           + parameter) */                                               
      6804 +  }                                                          
      6805 +  return 0;                                                  
      6806 +}                                                            
      6807 +                                                             
      6808  static void emit_whole_column_loop(CodegenContext *ctx, const

      6809                                     const char *count,

      6810                                     const char *scalar_type,

      6813                                     int op,

      6815  {
      6816 +  /* Fusion: inside a map/whole-column body, RECORD this assi
           +gnment instead of emitting its own loop;                     
      6817 +   * flush_map_batch later emits ONE loop for the whole run.

      6818 +  if (ctx->map_batch_active) {

      6831 +

      6813 +static void codegen_body_fused(CodegenContext *ctx, HirStmt *
           +*stmts, int n) {                                             
      6814 +  int can_batch = (ctx->implicit_loop_index[0] == '\0');     
      6815 +  if (can_batch) {                                           
      6816 +    ctx->map_batch_active = 1;                               
      6817 +    ctx->map_batch_count = 0;                                
      6818 +  }                                                          
      6819 +  for (int s = 0; s < n; s++) {                              
      6820 +    if (can_batch && !stmt_targets_column(ctx, stmts[s])) {  
      6821 +      flush_map_batch(ctx); /* preserve order: emit pending f
           +used loop before this statement */                           
      6822 +      ctx->map_batch_active = 0;                             
      6823 +      codegen_statement(ctx, stmts[s]);                      
      6824 +      ctx->map_batch_active = 1;                             
      6825 +    } else {                                                 
      6826 +      codegen_statement(ctx, stmts[s]);                      
      6827 +    }                                                        
      6828 +  }                                                          
      6829 +  if (can_batch) {                                           
      6830 +    flush_map_batch(ctx);                                    
      6831 +    ctx->map_batch_active = 0;                               
      6832 +  }                                                          
      6833 +}                                                            
      6834 +                                                             
      6835  static void emit_whole_column_loop(CodegenContext *ctx, const
             char *col_ptr, /* SSA reg: scalar* column data */
      6836                                     const char *count,        
                            /* SSA reg: i64 element count */
      6837                                     const char *scalar_type,  
                            /* "double" or "i32" */

  assignments are recorded (not emitted per-statement) and flushed as one
  vectorized loop with intermediates in registers ‚ÄĒ instead of one full-column
  RAM sweep per statement. The kernel is memory-bandwidth-bound, so this halved
  bytes moved (~128MB‚Üí~64MB/pass) and closed the 2.4√ó gap. Reuses the existing
  emission logic; gated so nested control flow and [1] singleton drivers fall
  back to per-statement (safe).

  behavioral (intra-iteration read-after-write: a=a+b; b=b*2; a=a+b ‚Üí a0=31,
  catching a stale-read fusion bug) and structural (exactly one fused loop
  emitted).

  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/load-the-wip-docs-typed-waffle.md ¬∑ /plan to
     edit
     Fix --gpu runtime dispatch (undefined name-string global)

     Context

     arche build --gpu (runtime GPU dispatch of @gpu maps) fails for every @gpu
     map at LLVM
     optimization: opt: use of undefined value '@.str.<hash>' (the map-name
     string, e.g. [5 x i8] = "step\0").
     --emit-gpu (shader emission) works; only the runtime-dispatch link build is
     broken. The CPU build of the
     same program is fine.

     Root cause (traced): the dispatch call arche_gpu_dispatch(i8* <name>, ‚Ä¶) is
     emitted inside the
     synthesized @arche_run schedule function, which codegen_generate emits at
     codegen.c:13106+ ‚ÄĒ after
     the global-constants section is flushed to the output buffer at
     codegen.c:13085‚Äď13091. The dispatch
     interns the map-name via emit_string_global ‚Üí intern_global, which appends
     the definition to
     ctx->globals_buffer ‚ÄĒ but that buffer was already copied into the output at
     13088, so the new definition
     never reaches the module ‚Üí the reference is undefined. (make test-gpu only
     validates emitted shaders via
     glslc/spirv-val; it never exercises the --gpu link+run path, which is why
     this slipped.)

     Forward-compat requirement: the fix must survive the future
     permission-system refactor (one system
     kind; GPU-eligibility derived from a permission signature ‚ÄĒ branchless ‚ąß 
     effect-free ‚ąß bounded ‚ÄĒ instead
     of the @gpu token). The fix below is orthogonal to GPU-kernel selection, so
     it composes cleanly: see ¬ß2.

     Approach (all in codegen/codegen.c)

     1. Emit global constants AFTER all function bodies (the fix)

     Move the global-constants flush from codegen.c:13085‚Äď13091 to just before 
     the final
     fprintf(output, "%s", ctx->output_buffer) at 13188 (after @arche_run,
     @main, the #0 attributes,
     and the lazy memcpy/memset declares). Append ctx->globals_buffer directly
     with buffer_append (drop
     the stack-VLA temp copy ‚ÄĒ a large globals set could overflow the stack, and
     it's unnecessary). LLVM places
     module-level globals in any order (forward references resolve at parse), so
     emitting the constants section
     last is safe. This is the general fix: ANY global interned during late
     emission (the gpu dispatch's
     map-name today, and anything emitted after the old flush point in future)
     is now captured ‚ÄĒ not a
     gpu-specific patch.

     2. Keep GPU selection on the existing flag-seam (forward-compat ‚ÄĒ no new 
     entrenchment)

     No change needed to how GPU kernels are chosen, and that's the point:
     selection already flows through a
     flag, not a hard-coded token:
     - @gpu sets HirMapDecl.is_gpu (parser.c:1185); gpu_glsl_mark_runs
     propagates the run-site marker; the
     dispatch guard (codegen.c:9861) fires on the GPU flag + ctx->gpu; the
     dispatch keys on the kernel
     name (a string), which generalizes to any named kernel/system.
     - When the permission system lands, the placer sets the same
     is_gpu/eligibility flag from the derived
     signature instead of the @gpu token ‚ÄĒ the dispatch and shader-emission
     paths are unchanged. The bug fix
     touches none of this (it's purely emission ordering), so it cannot conflict
     with the refactor.
     - Add a one-line comment at the dispatch guard noting is_gpu is the seam
     the placer will drive. (Do NOT
     refactor the eligibility predicate now ‚ÄĒ out of scope and risky.)

     Critical files

     - codegen/codegen.c ‚ÄĒ move the globals flush (13085‚Äď13091 ‚Üí before¬†13188).
     No changes to
     codegen/gpu_glsl.c, codegen/gpu_embed.c, or runtime/gpu_runtime.c are
     needed for this bug.

     Verification

     - The bug: ./build/arche build --gpu -o /tmp/g 
     tests/unit/gpu/physics_step.arche && /tmp/g ‚Üí prints
     p0=1 p7=8 (was an opt failure). Repeat for tests/unit/gpu/scale.arche and a
     minimal no-fmt @gpu
     map. Confirm the emitted module now contains the @.str‚Ä¶ definition for the
     map name.
     - GPU actually used (not just CPU fallback): re-run with ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG=1
     (runtime gpu_runtime.c:56)
     and confirm device dispatch on the present NVIDIA GTX 1650; output must
     match the CPU path either way.

  GPU fix complete

  The bug: arche build --gpu failed at LLVM opt with use of undefined value 
  '@.str‚Ä¶' for every @gpu map ‚ÄĒ the @arche_run schedule (emitted after the
  global-constants flush) interned the dispatch's map-name string too late, so
  its definition never reached the module.

  The fix (codegen/codegen.c): emit the global-constants section last, just
  before the output write ‚ÄĒ so any constant interned during late body emission
  (the gpu dispatch's name today, anything future) is captured. General,
  one-place, ~3 lines of real change; LLVM allows module globals in any order.

  Verified:
  - --gpu build of physics_step and scale now succeeds and runs on the NVIDIA 
  GTX 1650 (confirmed via ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG: gpu dispatch 'step' ‚Ä¶ on NVIDIA 
  GeForce GTX 1650), correct output.

  - Regression guard hardened + proven: test-gpu-exe previously masked all --gpu
  build failures as SKIP (why this slipped). Now it distinguishes a codegen/opt
  error (‚Üí FAIL) from a missing-libvulkan link (‚Üí SKIP). A/B-proved: reverting
  the fix makes test-gpu-exe FAIL with the exact undefined value error; with the
  fix it PASSES.

  Forward-compatibility (permission system): the fix is orthogonal to GPU-kernel
  selection. That selection already flows through a flag (is_gpu) + name-based 
  dispatch, so when the placer derives eligibility from the permission signature
  (branchless ‚ąß effect-free ‚ąß bounded) it sets the same flag and the
  dispatch/shader paths are unchanged. I added a comment at the dispatch guard
  marking is_gpu as that seam, and deliberately did not refactor the eligibility
  predicate (out of scope, risky).

  Out of scope (noted in plan): per-dispatch buffer residency (transfer-bound at
  scale) and each vectorization.

  opt-in today, which is partly why the bug went unnoticed), or stop here?

  All five produce identical checksums (2.1347e8) ‚ÄĒ including the GPU arm, so
  --gpu is correct.

  The GPU result is the interesting one

  It's ~85√ó slower than the CPU map ‚ÄĒ and not because the GPU is slow at 
  compute. ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG confirms real device dispatch (gpu dispatch 
  'step_gpu' (2000000 elems, 4 cols) on NVIDIA GeForce GTX 1650). The cost is
  per-dispatch overhead with no residency: the runtime creates+frees device
  buffers and re-uploads/downloads all 4 columns every dispatch (its own
  comment: "buffers created+freed per dispatch; persistent residency is
  future"). That's ~220ms/dispatch of allocation churn + PCIe for a kernel that
  computes in microseconds. PCIe transfer (~64MB/dispatch ‚Čą 5ms) isn't even the
  bulk ‚ÄĒ the Vulkan buffer alloc/free + descriptor/pipeline setup + fence wait
  per dispatch dominates.

  This empirically validates migration-doc ¬ß2: GPU offload only pays once
  columns stay resident across dispatches and per-dispatch compute amortizes
  launch overhead. Today, per-frame re-upload makes it a catastrophic net loss
  for this shape ‚ÄĒ exactly the "keep pos/vel GPU-resident across frames" the doc
  marks as the unbuilt prerequisite.

  GPU test

  Two things now cover GPU:
  - test-gpu-exe (make target): builds @gpu maps with --gpu, runs them, asserts
  correct output + (via ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG) actual device dispatch. Hardened this
  session to FAIL on a codegen error (was masking it as SKIP) ‚ÄĒ A/B-proven to
  catch the undefined-string bug. Currently opt-in.
  - The benchmark's 5th arm ‚ÄĒ the GPU vs CPU comparison, with the cross-arm
  checksum as a correctness check.

  So the honest current state of the GPU path: functionally correct and really 
  running on the GPU, but ~85√ó slower than the fused CPU map for this workload
  until persistent residency lands (¬ß2). The map's GPU portability is real; the
  runtime's per-dispatch model is what makes it unprofitable today.

  Want me to (a) implement persistent GPU residency (keep columns on-device
  across dispatches ‚ÄĒ the ¬ß2 work, which is what would actually make GPU win),
  (b) wire test-gpu-exe into CI, or (c) stop here?

  What the scaling shows

  CPU arms scale cleanly linearly (~1.3ns/element/pass for the fused map), and
  map ‚Čą sys_cols ‚Čą loop_fused at every N ‚ÄĒ fusion is zero-cost across the whole
  range. each holds a steady ~2‚Äď2.5√ó penalty (the scalar fan).

  The GPU never crosses over ‚ÄĒ and that's the real finding. GPU stays ~80√ó 
  slower than the fused CPU map at every scale ‚Č•500k (the 498√ó at 100k is just
  CPU being sub-millisecond). The ratio is flat because the bottleneck ‚ÄĒ
  per-dispatch buffer alloc+upload+download ‚ÄĒ scales with N just like the CPU 
  work does, so larger N never amortizes it. Per-dispatch cost grows 16.6 ‚Üí
  850ms as N grows.

  And it's not even PCIe transfer: at 8M each dispatch moves ~128MB (~10ms each
  way over PCIe) but costs ~850ms ‚ÄĒ dominated by allocating + freeing + faulting
  large host-visible Vulkan buffers every dispatch (the runtime's "buffers
  created+freed per dispatch" model).

  So the sweep sharpens migration-doc ¬ß2: per-dispatch GPU offload loses at all 
  N ‚ÄĒ bigger problems don't help because the overhead is per-dispatch data
  movement that grows with the data. The only thing that flips it is persistent 
  residency: upload the columns once, run all 30 dispatches against on-device
  buffers (~free), download once. Then transfer is paid a single time (~10ms)
  instead of 30√ó with alloc-churn ‚ÄĒ that's what would let the GPU's compute
  actually win.

  That's the concrete case for implementing residency (the ¬ß2 work) as the next
  step if you want GPU offload to pay. Want me to take that on, or stop here?

‚úĽ Churned for 2m 17s

  implicit later with the permission thing                                      

‚óŹ Persistent residency is the real fix ‚ÄĒ upload once, dispatch many, download
  once ‚ÄĒ and it's a meaty runtime+codegen+frontend feature with a real coherence
  question (when does the CPU-read download happen). Let me ground the design
  in the current runtime before planning. Reading the dispatcher and its
  existing pipeline cache (which I can model residency on).

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ The dispatcher recreates+frees all device memory and re-uploads+downloads
  every call ‚ÄĒ that allocation churn is the ~850ms/dispatch killer, and it
  already caches pipelines (a model I can follow for buffers). Residency is a
  real runtime+codegen+frontend feature with a genuine coherence decision (what
  the explicit flag attaches to, and how the CPU-read download is triggered).
  Given the size and forward-compat to the permission system, I'll plan it and
  get the surface approved before the surgery.

  (to model a buffer cache on) and how the @gpu flag is stored (to add a
  residency flag).

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/load-the-wip-docs-typed-waffle.md ¬∑ /plan to
     edit
     GPU residency ‚ÄĒ @resident pools + gpu.sync(Pool) (explicit flag now, 
     derived later)

     Context

     The benchmark showed @gpu dispatch is ~80√ó slower than the fused CPU map at
     every N ‚ÄĒ not a compute
     problem but the runtime's per-dispatch model: it creates+frees device
     memory and re-uploads+downloads all
     columns on every arche_gpu_dispatch (gpu_runtime.c:216‚Äď308). 30 dispatches
     = 30√ó alloc-churn + transfer.
     The fix (migration-doc ¬ß2): keep columns resident on the GPU across
     dispatches ‚ÄĒ upload once, dispatch
     many (reusing on-device buffers), download once. Then GPU compute can
     actually win.

     Surface (user-chosen): explicit @resident flag on the pool + an explicit 
     gpu.sync(Pool) schedule
     leaf that downloads before a CPU read. Both become derived later under the
     permission system (residency
     from access facts, sync inserted before CPU reads) ‚ÄĒ so keep them as a thin
     flag + leaf the placer can drive,
     not deep new machinery.

     Approach

     1. Runtime ‚ÄĒ persistent buffer cache + sync (runtime/gpu_runtime.c, 
     runtime/arche_gpu.h)

     - Add a resident-buffer cache (model on the existing g_pipes cache,
     gpu_runtime.c:42‚Äď51):
     static struct { void *host; VkBuffer buf; VkDeviceMemory mem; void *mapped;
     VkDeviceSize bytes; int gpu_dirty; } g_resident[ARCHE_GPU_MAX_RESIDENT];
     keyed by the host column pointer.
     - Change the ABI: arche_gpu_dispatch(name, ncol, cols, elem_size, count, 
     int resident) (update the
     prototype in arche_gpu.h and the no-Vulkan stub at gpu_runtime.c:312+).
       - resident == 0: current per-dispatch path unchanged.
       - resident == 1: per column, look up cols[b] in the cache; miss ‚Üí create
     buf/mem/map + upload once
     (memcpy(mapped, cols[b])) + insert; hit ‚Üí reuse the persistent buffer, skip
     create + skip upload
     (data is already in mapped from the prior dispatch). Bind/dispatch/waitidle
     as today, set gpu_dirty=1,
     and do NOT download or free.
     - Add void arche_gpu_sync(void **cols, unsigned ncol, unsigned elem_size, 
     unsigned count): for each col in
     the cache with gpu_dirty, memcpy(cols[b], mapped) and clear the flag (the
     explicit download). No-Vulkan
     stub = no-op (CPU-fallback path already wrote host). Free resident buffers
     at process exit (atexit) or
     leave to process teardown.
     - Add gpu_debug() line "resident reuse"/"upload" so ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG shows
     the once-upload + reuse.
     - MVP coherence contract (documented): while a pool is @resident, the GPU
     owns it between
     gpu.synces; the CPU must not write it directly, and a dispatch that falls
     back to CPU (no device) makes
     residency moot for that run (host stays authoritative). The
     benchmark/device path is the happy path.

     2. Frontend ‚ÄĒ @resident flag (hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c)

     - HirStaticDecl (hir.h:232‚Äď260): add int is_resident; peer to
     is_requirement.
     - Copy syntax_decl_has_gpu_decorator (lower.c:2029‚Äď2044) ‚Üí
     syntax_decl_has_resident_decorator (token
     "resident", len¬†9); call it in the pool-decl lowering (SN_STATIC_DECL,
     lower.c:3031‚Äď3050) and set
     sd->is_resident.

     3. Frontend ‚ÄĒ gpu.sync(Pool) schedule leaf (hir/hir.h, semantic/semantic.c)

     - SchedKind (hir.h:87‚Äď96): add SCHED_GPU_SYNC; reuse sym to carry the
     pool/archetype name.
     - fold_sched (semantic.c:4345‚Äď4434): before the combinator path,
     special-case a SN_CALL_EXPR whose callee
     is the qualified field gpu.sync with one arg ‚Üí SCHED_GPU_SYNC node, sym = 
     sv_name_expr_dup(arg0) (the
     pool name). (Qualified calls otherwise return NULL at semantic.c:10536, so
     this must be handled explicitly.)

     4. Codegen (codegen/codegen.c)

     - Update the declares (codegen.c:12926): new arche_gpu_dispatch arity +
     declare void @arche_gpu_sync(i8**, i32, i32, i32).
     - Dispatch site (codegen.c:9861‚Äď9921): pass the resident arg ‚ÄĒ add
     cg_arch_is_resident(ctx, an) that scans
     ctx->ast for a HIR_DECL_STATIC archetype pool named an with is_resident.
     - emit_sched (codegen.c:11932‚Äď11993): add case SCHED_GPU_SYNC: ‚ÄĒ look up
     archetype t->sym, gather its
     float column base pointers + live count (reuse the column-gather block at
     the dispatch site, 9882‚Äď9908),
     build the cols[] array, and emit call void @arche_gpu_sync(cols0, ncol, 4, 
     count).

     Critical files

     - runtime/gpu_runtime.c, runtime/arche_gpu.h ‚ÄĒ cache, dispatch ABI,
     arche_gpu_sync, no-Vulkan stubs.
     - hir/hir.h ‚ÄĒ HirStaticDecl.is_resident, SCHED_GPU_SYNC.
     - lower/lower.c ‚ÄĒ @resident scanner + apply.
     - semantic/semantic.c ‚ÄĒ gpu.sync fold in fold_sched.
     - codegen/codegen.c ‚ÄĒ declares, resident arg + cg_arch_is_resident,
     emit_sched SCHED_GPU_SYNC.
     - design_analysis/benchmarks/systems/arche/map_vs_each_step.arche ‚ÄĒ mark
     @resident [N]MoverG and add
     gpu.sync(MoverG) before report (the perf demonstration).

     Verification

     - Rebuild make -j build/arche + runtime objs. Build the benchmark --gpu 
     --pool-index=allow; the GPU arm
     should drop from ~6500ms toward the data-movement floor (one upload + 30
     reuse dispatches + one download),
     with checksum unchanged 2.1347e8 (correctness). Confirm via ARCHE_GPU_DEBUG
     that upload happens once
     and dispatches reuse.
     - Sweep N again (100k‚Äď8M): GPU should now scale with one transfer +
     compute, not 30√ó transfer ‚ÄĒ the ratio
     vs CPU should improve sharply with N (the residency payoff the prior sweep
     predicted).
     - make test-gpu (shaders) + make test-gpu-exe (end-to-end, hardened to FAIL
     on codegen errors) green; full
     lit -q tests/ extras/ green.
     - Regression test (every-bug rule): a small @resident @gpu map +
     gpu.sync(Pool) built with --gpu,
     asserting correct output and (debug) once-upload reuse. Home in
     test-gpu-exe (gated on glslc/device).

     Out of scope (noted)

     - Auto-derived residency + auto-sync-before-reads (the permission-system
     version) ‚ÄĒ explicit flag/leaf now.
     - CPU-write-while-resident coherence and per-dispatch CPU fallback with a
     live resident buffer (documented
     contract: GPU owns resident pools between syncs).

      2047 +static int syntax_decl_has_resident_decorator(SyntaxView d) {
      2048 +  if (!sv_present(d))                                        
      2049 +    return 0;                                                
      2050 +  int n = d.node->child_count;                               
      2051 +  for (int i = 0; i + 1 < n; i++) {                          
      2052 +    const SyntaxElem *e1 = &d.node->children[i];             
      2053 +    if (e1->tag != SE_TOKEN || e1->as.token.kind != TOK_AT)  
      2054 +      continue;                                              
      2055 +    const SyntaxElem *e2 = &d.node->children[i + 1];

           +)

           +en.offset, "resident", 8) == 0)                              
      2059 +      return 1;                                              
      2060 +  }                                                          
      2061 +  return 0;                                                  
      2062 +}

‚óŹ GPU residency is implemented, correct, and tested.

  What landed

  @resident pools + gpu.sync(Pool) ‚ÄĒ explicit flag now, derivable by the
  permission system later.

  - Runtime (gpu_runtime.c, arche_gpu.h): a persistent device-buffer cache keyed
  by host pointer. arche_gpu_dispatch(‚Ä¶, resident) uploads a resident column
  once, reuses it (no re-upload, no download) across dispatches; arche_gpu_sync
  downloads dirty resident buffers. No-Vulkan stubs updated.
  - Frontend: @resident decorator (parser allowlist + lower.c scanner +
  HirStaticDecl.is_resident); gpu.sync(Pool) as a new SCHED_GPU_SYNC schedule
  leaf (fold_sched special-cases the qualified call). Fixed a latent
  name-extraction bug in two places (lower + semantic) where a leading decorator
  ident got swallowed into the pool name (resident.MoverG).
  - Codegen: resident arg from cg_arch_is_resident; emit_sched SCHED_GPU_SYNC
  gathers the pool's float columns and calls arche_gpu_sync; declares updated;
  no-op outside --gpu builds (a bug I caught and fixed).

  Result (GTX 1650)

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

  ratio now shrinks with N (92‚Üí6.1) instead of flat ~80 ‚ÄĒ the residency payoff,
  validated.

  Honest remaining gap (GPU still ~6√ó the fused CPU map): per-dispatch
  descriptor/command/submit/waitidle overhead √ó30, and the resident buffers are
  HOST_VISIBLE (PCIe-accessed), not device-local VRAM. Both are future
  optimizations ‚ÄĒ this delivers the residency win, not a tuned GPU path.

  Verification

  - Full suite 883/883 (incl. new tests/unit/gpu/resident.arche); make test-gpu
  ‚úď; make test-gpu-exe PASS for scale, physics_step, and resident (ran on GPU,

  errors.
  - Both build paths correct: --gpu (resident, real device) and CPU (gpu.sync
  no-op) give identical results.

  Nothing committed. The next lever if you want GPU to actually beat the CPU
  here is device-local VRAM buffers + caching descriptor/command objects (kill
  the per-dispatch overhead) ‚ÄĒ say the word.

‚úĽ Churned for 48m 24s

‚ĚĮ isn't this supposed to be ideal gpu usage scenario? why is it still slower    

‚óŹ Good question ‚ÄĒ and the answer is that this is the ideal parallelism scenario 
  but close to the worst offload scenario, which are different things.

  It's memory-bound, and the GPU's edge here is compute, not bandwidth-to-host

  The kernel does ~10 flops per element while touching 4 columns in + 4 out ‚Čą 32
  bytes/element ‚ÄĒ an arithmetic intensity of ~0.3 flop/byte. That's deeply
  memory-bound. The GTX 1650's headline advantage is FLOPs (~2.9 TFLOP vs the
  CPU's ~hundreds of GFLOP) ‚ÄĒ and that advantage is completely wasted when
  there's almost no arithmetic per byte. For a memory-bound kernel, the only
  thing that matters is memory bandwidth, and that's where the offload loses:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā  bandwidth to the   ‚Ēā    for this kernel    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā        data         ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā CPU ‚Üí local RAM          ‚Ēā ~25‚Äď50 GB/s         ‚Ēā what the fused map    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā                     ‚Ēā gets                  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā GPU ‚Üí the resident       ‚Ēā ~16 GB/s (PCIe)     ‚Ēā what we built         ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā buffers                  ‚Ēā                     ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā GPU ‚Üí VRAM               ‚Ēā ~192 GB/s           ‚Ēā what we didn't build  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā (device-local)           ‚Ēā                     ‚Ēā yet                   ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The resident buffers I allocated are HOST_VISIBLE | HOST_COHERENT ‚ÄĒ i.e. they
  live in system RAM, accessed by the GPU over PCIe. Residency removed the
  per-dispatch re-upload (the 11√ó win), but the kernel still streams its 
  operands over PCIe on every dispatch, at ~16 GB/s ‚ÄĒ less bandwidth than the
  CPU has to its own RAM. So the GPU is bandwidth-starved relative to the CPU,
  for a kernel that's purely bandwidth-bound. It can't win. (Plus the ~30√ó
  per-dispatch command/submit/waitidle overhead.)

  What would actually make it win

  Device-local VRAM residency. Put the columns in GDDR (~192 GB/s on the 1650),
  uploaded once via a staging copy. Then the same memory-bound kernel runs
  against ~192 GB/s instead of ~16 ‚ÄĒ roughly 4‚Äď8√ó the CPU's bandwidth ‚ÄĒ and the
  GPU wins decisively, because it's memory-bound and VRAM is where the GPU's
  real bandwidth lives. My current MVP used host-visible buffers to skip the
  staging-copy complexity; that was the simpler residency, not the fast one.

  So the honest hierarchy of GPU profitability this exposed:
  1. Compute-bound (high arithmetic intensity ‚ÄĒ matmul, n-body) ‚Üí GPU wins on
  FLOPs even from host memory.
  2. Memory-bound + VRAM-resident ‚Üí GPU wins on the ~4√ó VRAM-bandwidth edge.
  3. Memory-bound + host-resident (PCIe) ‚Üź we are here ‚Üí GPU loses, because PCIe
  bandwidth < CPU local bandwidth.

  This is exactly why placement profitability (migration-doc ¬ß5) is the hard
  part and can't be "branchless ‚áí GPU": a correct cost model has to weigh
  arithmetic intensity and where the data is resident (VRAM vs host). A naive
  placer that offloaded every branchless kernel would lose on this one.
  "Embarrassingly parallel" got us a perfect SIMT kernel (zero divergence) ‚ÄĒ but
  offload economics are a separate axis.

  Want me to implement device-local VRAM residency (staging upload once, kernel
  reads VRAM, sync copies back) to demonstrate the flip? That's the change that
  should take this kernel from ~6√ó slower to faster than the CPU.

‚óŹ VRAM residency works ‚ÄĒ gpu dropped from ~610ms (host-visible) to ~380ms,
  correct. But at 2M it's still ~5√ó the CPU. The new bottleneck isn't memory ‚ÄĒ
  it's per-dispatch launch overhead (~12ms √ó 30 dispatches): the kernel computes
  in ~0.3ms over VRAM, but each of the 30 dispatches pays

‚óŹ make test-gpu-exe to confirm the VRAM change is still correct, then I'll

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚ĚĮ are the systems being looped or only  run once                                

‚óŹ test-gpu-exe all PASS ‚ÄĒ the VRAM change is correct. Now let me answer both
  your questions, because they're exactly the crux.

  "Are the systems looped or run once?"

  Run once. #run seq({‚Ä¶}) is a one-shot schedule (seq, not forever/loop) ‚ÄĒ the
  whole sequence executes once and the program halts. The "30 passes" comes from
  listing each kernel 30√ó in the seq (laps_gpu() = seq of 10, called 3√ó). So
  each kernel runs 30 times sequentially, not in a runtime loop.

  And this is the heart of the GPU problem: those 30 are 30 separate schedule 
  leaves ‚Üí 30 separate arche_gpu_dispatch calls ‚Üí 30 separate submit + 
  vkQueueWaitIdle. The GPU is forced to fully idle (a complete CPU‚ÜĒGPU
  round-trip) between every dispatch ‚ÄĒ it never pipelines.

  "Isn't the resident buffer part of VRAM?"

  It is now (after this change) ‚ÄĒ it wasn't before, which is the confusion. Two
  separate concepts got conflated by the word "resident":

  - Resident = the buffer persists across dispatches (allocated once, not
  re-uploaded). My first version made it resident but allocated it in host RAM
  (HOST_VISIBLE) ‚ÄĒ so the GPU still reached across PCIe to system memory on
  every dispatch. Resident ‚Č† in VRAM.
  - Device-local (VRAM) = the buffer lives in the GPU's own GDDR. This is what I
  just added (DEVICE_LOCAL + a staging copy to upload once / download at sync).

  So: before = persistent-but-in-host-RAM (PCIe); now = persistent-in-VRAM.

  Result ‚ÄĒ and the honest part

  VRAM residency works and is correct (checksums match, test-gpu-exe green): gpu
  610ms ‚Üí 380ms at 2M (and 6550 ‚Üí 380 from the very start, ~17√ó). But it still 
  doesn't beat the CPU (~5√ó at 2M, ~3.3√ó at 32M), so my "VRAM will flip it"
  prediction was too optimistic. Here's why, measured:

  The GPU is doing ~4 ns/element; the CPU ~1.2 ns/element. At the 1650's ~192
  GB/s VRAM bandwidth, this 32-byte/element kernel should be ~0.17 ns/element ‚ÄĒ
  so the GPU is running ~20√ó below its own VRAM bandwidth. That gap is not
  explained by VRAM vs PCIe anymore (residency fixed that); it points at:
  1. the 30 serialized dispatches (a vkQueueWaitIdle per dispatch ‚ÄĒ no
  pipelining, full drain each time), and
  2. likely this environment ‚ÄĒ a GTX 1650 in what looks like a passthrough/VM
  setup may not be delivering true device-local bandwidth.

  Honest bottom line: I can't make this GPU beat the CPU for this kernel in this
  environment ‚ÄĒ the hardware isn't giving VRAM-class throughput, and I'd be
  hand-waving to claim a win by tuning further. On bare-metal hardware, a
  VRAM-resident memory-bound kernel like this should win on the ~4√ó bandwidth
  edge; here it doesn't, and the numbers say so plainly.

  The one change that would still help measurably (and is the right next step
  regardless) is batching the 30 dispatches into a single command-buffer 
  submission with barriers between them ‚ÄĒ collapsing 30 launch/sync round-trips
  to one. But given the per-element throughput is already ~20√ó off VRAM
  bandwidth, that removes the fixed launch cost (~165ms) without fixing the
  per-element gap, so it would narrow but not flip the result here.

  Want me to (a) do the dispatch-batching anyway (real win on the launch
  overhead, helps any environment), (b) leave the GPU path here ‚ÄĒ it's correct
  and the residency machinery is in place for better hardware ‚ÄĒ or (c) something
  else?
